____________ kathy snowden city clerktreasurer preface this a republication of the general and permanent ordinances of the city of valley alabama source materials used in the preparation of the the 2001 ordinances and subsequent ordinances adopted by the city council the source of each section is included in the history note appearing in parentheses at the end thereof the absence of such a note indicates that the section is new and was adopted for the first time with the adoption of the use of the comparative tables appearing in the back of this the reader can locate any ordinance included herein the chapters of the been conveniently arranged in alphabetical order and the various sections within each chapter have been catchlined to facilitate usage notes which tie related sections of the which refer to relevant state law have been included a table listing the state law citations and setting forth their location within the included at the back of this system the chapter and section numbering system used in this the same system used in many state and local government codes each section number consists of two parts separated by a dash the figure before the dash refers to the chapter number and the figure after the dash refers to the position of the section within the chapter thus the second section of chapter 1 is numbered 12 and the first section of chapter 6 is 61 under this system each section is identified with its chapter and at the same time new sections can be inserted in their proper place by using the decimal system for amendments for example if new material consisting of one section that would logically come between sections 61 and 62 is desired to be added such new section would be numbered 615 new articles and new divisions may be included in the same way or in the case of articles may be placed at the end of the chapter embracing the subject and in the case of divisions may be placed at the end of the article embracing the subject the next successive number shall be assigned to the new article or division new chapters may be included by using one of the reserved chapter numbers care should be taken that the alphabetical arrangement of chapters is maintained when including new chapters page numbering system the page numbering system used in this a prefix system the letters to the left of the colon are an abbreviation which represents a certain portion of the volume the number to the right of the colon represents the number of the page in that portion in the case of a chapter of the the number to the left of the colon indicates the number of the chapter in the case of an appendix to the the letter immediately to the left of the colon indicates the letter of the appendix the following are typical parts of codes of ordinances which may or may not appear in this this time and their corresponding prefixes code cd code appendix cda1 code comparative tables cct1 state law reference table slt1 code index cdi1 index the index has been prepared with the greatest of care each particular item has been placed under several headings some of which are couched in lay phraseology others in legal terminology and still others in language generally used by local government officials and employees there are numerous cross references within the index itself which stand as guideposts to direct the user to the particular item in which the user is interested looseleaf supplements a special feature of this publication is the looseleaf system of binding and supplemental servicing of the publication with this system the publication will be kept uptodate subsequent amendatory legislation will be properly edited and the affected page or pages will be reprinted these new pages will be distributed to holders of copies of the publication with instructions for the manner of inserting the new pages and deleting the obsolete pages keeping this publication uptodate at all times will depend largely upon the holder of the publication as revised pages are received it will then become the responsibility of the holder to have the amendments inserted according to the attached instructions it is strongly recommended by the publisher that all such amendments be inserted immediately upon receipt to avoid misplacing them and in addition that all deleted pages be saved and filed for historical reference purposes reference authority to adopt code of ordinances ala 197  11457 definitions and rules of construction in the construction of this of all ordinances the following rules shall be observed  provided however that these rules of construction shall not be applied to any section of this any ordinance which contains any express provisions excluding such construction or where the subject matter or content of such section may be repugnant thereto bond when a bond is required an undertaking in writing is sufficient city officials officers and employees whenever reference is made to officials boards commissions departments officers employees or agencies by title only this shall be construed as though followed by the words of the city of valley and shall be taken to mean the official board commission department officer employee or agency of this city having the title mentioned or performing the duties indicated  and powers and authority granted to them shall be deemed to be grants of such powers and authority to their respective duly designated subordinates city this city in the city the term the city this city or in the city shall mean the city of valley alabama  and shall include any duly authorized officer or employee if the context so admits every section contained in this whether expressed to apply in the city or not so expressed shall apply and have full force and effect within the corporate limits of the city and within its police jurisdiction and within the territorial limits of any property or rightofway owned by the city wherever situated  provided however that any such section shall not apply within the police jurisdiction if expressed to apply within the corporate limits of the city or if the same cannot legally be made to apply in the police jurisdiction or if the same cannot physically apply in the police jurisdiction or if the same otherwise than by use of such term as in the city or within the city contains clear inherent evidence of intent that it shall not apply in the police jurisdiction the term  or this  is referred to without further qualification it shall mean the ordinances city of valley alabama as designated in section 11 ala whenever reference is made to the ala or the ala 197 it shall mean the alabama 197 as amended or any subsequent code of this state computation of time the time within which any act is provided by law or ordinance to be done must be computed by excluding the first day and including the last however if the last day is sunday or a legal holiday as defined in ala 197  138 or a day on which the office in which the act must be done shall close as permitted by any law of this state the last day also must be excluded and the next succeeding secular or working day shall be counted as the last day within which the act may be done state law reference computation of time ala 197  114 council city council the terms council and city council shall mean the city council of the city of valley alabama county the term county or this county shall mean chambers county alabama gender words used in the masculine gender include the feminine and neuter state law reference gender ala 197  112 health officer the term health officer shall mean the county health officer or his authorized representative joint authority all words giving a joint authority to three or more persons or officers of this in boldface type are intended as mere catchwords to indicate the contents of the section and shall not be deemed or taken to be titles of such sections nor as any part of the section nor unless expressly so provided shall they be so deemed when any of such sections including the catchlines are amended or reenacted no provision of this be held invalid by reason of deficiency in any such catchline or in any heading or title to any chapter article or division history notes the history notes appearing in parentheses after sections in this not intended to have any legal effect but are merely intended to indicate the source of matter contained in the sections editors notes and references the editors notes cross references and state law references in this not intended to have any legal effect but are merely intended to assist the user of this   effect of repeal of an ordinance a no new ordinance shall be construed or held to repeal a former ordinance whether such former ordinance is expressly repealed or not as to any offense committed against such former ordinance or as to any act done any penalty forfeiture or punishment so incurred or any right accrued or claim arising under the former ordinance or in any way whatever to affect any such offense or act so committed or so done or any penalty forfeiture or punishment so incurred or any right accrued or claim arising before the new ordinance takes effect save only that the proceedings thereafter shall conform to the ordinance in force at the time of such proceeding so far as practicable if any penalty forfeiture or punishment be mitigated by any provision of a new ordinance such provision may be by the consent of the party affected applied to any judgment announced after the new ordinance takes effect b the repeal of an ordinance shall not revive any ordinances in force before or at the time the ordinance repealed took effect c this section shall extend to all repeals either by express words or implication whether the repeal is in the ordinance making any new provisions upon the same subject or in any other ordinance d nothing contained in this be construed as abating any action pending on the effective date of this or by virtue of any general ordinance of the city herein repealed  or as discontinuing abating modifying or altering any penalty accrued or to accrue or as affecting the liability of any person or as waiving any right of the city under any ordinance or provision thereof in force on the effective date of this   severability it is hereby declared to be the intention of the council that the sections paragraphs sentences clauses and phrases of this all ordinances are severable and if any phrase clause sentence paragraph or section of this any ordinance or its application to any persons or circumstances shall be declared invalid by the valid judgment or decree of any court of competent jurisdiction such judgment or decree shall not affect the validity or enforceability of any of the remaining phrases clauses sentences paragraphs and sections or their application of this any ordinance state law reference severability of provisions of statutes ala 197  1116 amendment of a all ordinances passed subsequent to this amend repeal or in any way affect this be numbered in accordance with the numbering system of this printed for inclusion in this regard to repealed chapters articles divisions or sections or any part thereof by subsequent ordinances such repealed portions may be excluded from the omission from reprinted pages affected thereby any and all additions and amendments to this when passed in such form as to indicate the intention of the council to make the addition or amendment a part hereof shall be deemed to be incorporated in this so that reference to the be understood and intended to include such additions and amendments b amendments to any of the provisions of this be made by specific reference to the section number of this the deletion any part of this to insert or delete pages or portions thereof or to alter or tamper with this any manner whatsoever which will cause the law of the city to be misrepresented general penalty a any person firm or corporation committing an offense within the corporate limits of the city or within its police jurisdiction in violation of a provision of the ordinances of this city now existing or hereafter enacted shall upon conviction be punishable by a fine or not less than $5000 nor more than $50000 in addition any person so convicted may also be imprisoned or sentenced to hard labor for the city for a period not exceeding six months the penalty imposed upon a corporation shall consist of the fine only plus court cost no penalty shall consist of a fine or sentence of imprisonment exceeding the maximum fine or sentence of imprisonment established under state law for the commission of a substantially similar offense b should any civil action be brought to abate any violation the violating party shall also be liable to the city for all costs incurred by the city in enforcing such abatement including attorneys fees and costs c each day during which any violation continues shall be considered a separate offense  3231981   violations of state law a any person committing an offense within the corporate limits of the city or within its police jurisdiction which is declared by any law of the state now existing or hereafter enacted to be a misdemeanor shall be guilty of an offense against the city b any person committing an offense within the corporate limits of the city or within its police jurisdiction which is declared by any law of the state now existing or hereafter enacted to be a violation shall be guilty of an offense against the city c any person committing within the corporate limits of the city or within its police jurisdiction an offense as defined by ala 197  13a12 which offense is not declared by any law of the state now existing or hereafter enacted to be a felony misdemeanor or violation shall be guilty of an offense against the city d any person found to be in violation of subsection a b or c of this section shall upon conviction be punished by a fine of not less than $100 nor more than $50000 andor may be imprisoned or sentenced to hard labor for the city for a period not exceeding six months at the discretion of the court trying the case unless otherwise provided by subsection e or f of this section e any person found to be in violation of ala 197  325a191 pertaining to driving under the influence of alcohol controlled substances etc shall upon conviction be punished by a fine of not more than $500000 andor may be imprisoned or sentenced to hard labor for not more than one year unless otherwise provided by subsection f of this section f the penalty imposed upon a corporation shall consist of the fine only plus costs of court g each day during which any violation described in this section continues shall be considered a separate offense  3281994 state law reference enforcement of ordinances ala 197  11451  penalties for violations of ordinances ala 197  11459  abatement of nuisances ala 197  1147117 et seq  driving under influence of alcohol controlled substances etc ala 197  325a191 violation of orders rules and regulations any person who shall violate or fail neglect or refuse to comply with any lawful order of any lawful officer of the city made in pursuance of and under such officers authority as such or who shall violate or shall fail neglect or refuse to comply with any of the rules and regulations or laws adopted by this shall be guilty of an offense  provided however the provisions of this section shall not apply to violations of official duty imposed by this officers or employees of the city as such unless the provision imposing the duty also expressly makes the violation thereof unlawful or punishable presumption of responsibility the occupant of any premises and the owner of unoccupied premises upon which a violation of any provision of this any ordinance is apparent the owner of any object or material placed or remaining anywhere in violation thereof and the occupant and owner of any premises served by any excavation connection or structure illegally made or erected shall be deemed prima facie responsible for the violation so evidenced and subject to the sportsplex at 130 sportsplex drive valley alabama is established as the central of voting for all seven districts  3292004 qualification fees a a qualification fee is in the amount of $5000 is hereby the general fund of the city at a prior to the time of taking out qualification papers by any such candidates d any person desiring to qualify who is not financially able to pay the required fee may manager authority and duties the city manager shall have the authority and be charged with the duties set forth under ala 197  114321 as well as any other duties assigned him by the mayor or city council  term the term of the city manager shall be coextensive with the term of office of the councilmembers  provided however that he may be discharged upon 60 days written notice following the vote of at least twothirds of the entire number of members of the city council  compensation for his services the city manager shall be paid such salary as the council may by ordinance prescribe which salary shall be paid in 12 equal monthly installments as required by ala 197  114321a the compensation due to be paid may not be changed or altered during the city managers tenure unless otherwise authorized by the council  secs 21042120  reserved division 3  indemnity footnotes  3  state law reference indemnity ala 197  114724 scope a the city agrees to pay on behalf of all members of boards elected and appointed officials and employees of the city all sums which the members of boards elected and appointed officials and employees of the city become legally obligated to pay as damages because of negligence proximately causing bodily injury property damage or negligent and wrongful acts not intentional willful or wanton caused by an occurrence arising out of and in the line and scope of their legal duties or employment the city council shall have the right and duty to defend any suit against the members of boards elected and appointed officials and employees of the city which suit seeks damages on account of such negligent or wrongful acts performed in the line and scope of their duties such payments shall include court costs and attorneys fees b no independent contractor or volunteer shall be deemed a member of boards elected and appointed officials or employee of the city under any provision of this division and is specifically excluded from any obligation of the city imposed therein  4281986 limitation period a any person or entity having a claim or demand against members of boards elected and appointed officials and employees of the city shall file notice of the claim in the office of the city clerk within the applicable limitation period provided in ala 197  114723 b this division shall be personal to the indemnitee and liability under this division shall cease if legal action on the claim or demand or settlement effected is not filed in a court of competent jurisdiction within the applicable limitation period as provided in ala 197  6230 et seq  4281986 assignability of rights and privileges no rights under this division accruing to the benefit of any members of boards elected and appointed officials and employees of the city shall be assignable to any other person or entity  provided however that such rights and benefits shall descend to and be enforceable by the personal representative of a deceased board member elected or appointed official or employee of the city  4281986 payment of judgment of punitive damages  contributory negligence a no obligation of the city under this division shall be imposed on the city for payment of any judgment of punitive damages or for payment of costs or attorneys fee for any claim or demand based upon or growing out of any intentional willful or wanton act by a board member elected or appointed official or employee of the city in connection with performance of his legal duties or line and scope of his employment b the city shall incur no liability to any person or entity guilty of contributory negligence assumption of risk or consent at the time and place of the occurrence made the basis of the claim or demand  4281986 personal liability insurers the city shall not be obligated under this division to indemnify the personal liability insurer of a board member elected or appointed official or employee of the city for any sums such insurer may be obligated to pay further no obligation shall be imposed or incurred by the city under this division until or unless the personal liability insurer has paid all sums it is obligated to pay on behalf of its insured as an occurrence within the terms and conditions of its policy coverage or limits  4281986 waiving governmental immunity  settlement of claims a by enactment of this division the city does not waive any governmental immunity it may have so as to permit a direct suit against it in state court not available to a claimant under state statutory or case law b no liability of the city shall be incurred for settlement of any claim or demand without the consent of the city if entered without suit or entered pending trial but prior to judgment no liability for costs of appeal to the appropriate appellate court of this state or of the united states including additional attorneys fees and costs shall be imposed or incurred by the city unless the city shall consent to the appeal provided that the appeal footnotes  1  cross reference environment ch 30 state law reference animals ala 197  311 et seq  municipal regulation of dogs and cats ala 197  37a14  animals at large impoundment ala 197  1147110  municipal powers as to health cleanliness sanitation quarantine ala 197  1147130 et seq  cruelty to animals ala 197  13a1114 article i  in general secs 1011030  reserved article ii  animal control purpose of article the purpose of this article is to promote harmonious relations in the interaction between man and animal by 1 protecting animals from improper use abuse neglect exploitation inhumane treatment and health hazards  2 delineating the animal owners responsibility for the acts and behavior of his animal at all times  3 providing security to residents from annoyance intimidation injury and health hazards by animals  4 encouraging responsible pet ownership  5 providing standards for any and all persons and agencies public or private engaged in confinement buying selling harboring or dealing in animals in any manner whatsoever within the corporate limits of the city  and 6 ensuring the physical safety of humans  2141994 definitions the following words terms and phrases when used in this article shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning animal means any animal which is required by state law to be inoculated for rabies animal at large means when an animal is in any public street alley park or other public grounds or when off the premises of the owner or person who has custody of the animal and not constrained by a leash or under the immediate control of the owner or person who has custody of the animal animal bite means to be seized with the teeth or jaws so that a person or animal has been nipped gripped wounded or pierced and saliva of the biting animal has contacted the resulting break or abrasion of the skin animal control officer means any agent designated by the city council the city clerk or the chief of police to enforce this article animal shelter means a facility designated by the city council and used to temporarily confine and house animals that have been seized complaint means any written or oral report of an incident or condition alleged to be in violation of this article dangerous animal means any animal of potential danger that is known to be of a bad temperament toward humans or is known to have behaved in a threatening manner without provocation toward humans domestic animal means an animal species which association with man has been bred to a degree which has resulted in changes affecting the temperament color conformation or other attributes of the species to an extent that makes them unique and different from wild individuals of their kind exotic animals mean animals that dont occur naturally either presently or historically in the united states exposed to rabies means seized with the teeth or claws so that the skin of the person or animal seized has been nipped or gripped or has been wounded or pierced and includes suspected or confirmed contact of saliva with a break or abrasion of the skin or with any mucous membrane as determined by a licensed physician guard dog means a dog which is trained or used for the express purpose of protecting and guarding property guide dog means a dog especially trained for the purpose that is used as a guide to ambulation by a person who is totally or partially blind hearing dog means a dog especially trained for the purpose that is used as a guide to ambulation by a person who is hearing impaired licensed veterinarian means a veterinarian duly licensed to practice veterinary medicine in the state livestock and farm animals mean any animal that is considered livestock or a farm animal such as chickens horses mares jacks jennies colts cows calves yearlings bulls oxen sheep goats lambs kinds hogs shoats and pigs mauling means a serious injury inflicted by an animal to a human or another animal a mauling is differentiated from a bite by the degree of injury serious injury differentiates a bite from a mauling native animals mean animals that occur naturally either presently or historically in the united states and its territories in addition native wild animals include those animals introduced into the united states that have become widespread and are generally considered native neutered means made incapable of sexually reproducing offspring male animals nuisance means animals that 1 are allowed to act or perform in such a manner as to cause damage or unsanitary conditions to public property or to the property of another  2 enter any place where food is stored prepared served or sold to the public except guide dogs that are accompanying a totally or partially blind person and hearing dogs that accompany a hearing impaired person  3 chase run after or jump at vehicles using public streets or alleys  4 habitually snap growl snarl jump upon or otherwise threaten persons who are lawfully sing public sidewalks streets alleys parks recreation fields or other public places  5 habitually attack other animals  6 feed from turn over or otherwise disturb garbage containers  7 scratch or dig in flower beds gardens or soil or animals that damage the property of persons other than the owner  8 are allowed to mate in full or partial view of the public except for animals inside enclosures designed to keep mating from unwanted public viewing  9 disturb the peace by constantly or incessantly barking or howling or by constantly or incessantly making other disturbing noises owner means any person having a right of property in the animal or who keeps or harbors the animal or who has it in his care or acts as its custodian or who permits the animal to remain on or about any premises occupied by him restraint means when any of the following conditions exist 1 the animal is confined in a building or fenced pen or yard excluding electronic fences on its owners property or on the property of another person with the other persons consent adequate to prevent contact with the general public or any persons who enter the premises with the actual or implied permission of the owner or keeper of the animal persons presently using electronic fences at the time of adoption of this ordinance shall be allowed to continue to do so provided they register with the city clerk within 30 days of adoption of this ordinance provided further that should the fence not contain the animal and any complaint be made to the city this grandfathered status shall be lost and full compliance required 2 the animal when off the premises of the owner is under the immediate and effective control of a responsible person adequately restrained by leash sufficient to prevent the animal from engaging any other human or animal spayed means made incapable of sexually reproducing offspring female animals stray means any dog or cat not tagged with a rabies inoculation tag andor city registration tag andor personal identification tag vaccination means the administration of antirabies vaccines or other vaccines by the county rabies officer his authorized representative or any licensed veterinarian at such intervals as required by state law vicious animal means any animal of any species domestic or wild native or exotic that is known to have 1 a known propensity tendency or disposition to attack to cause injury or otherwise endanger the safety of human beings or animals as evidenced by habitual or repeated chasing snapping or barking at human beings or domestic animals or in a vicious or terrorizing manner approaching any person in an apparent attitude of attack whether or not the attack is actually consummated or capable of being consummated  or 2 attacks a human being or other domestic animal without provocation  provided that a dog shall not be deemed vicious if the threat injury or damage was sustained by a person who at the time was committing a willful trespass or other tort upon the premises occupied by the owner or keeper of the dog or was teasing tormenting abusing or assaulting the dog or has in the past abused or assaulted the dog or was committing or attempting to commit a crime  or 3 any animal which according to the records of the appropriate authority has inflicted injury on a human being without provocation  or 4 any animal which according to the records of the appropriate authority has killed a domestic animal without provocation while off the owners property  or 5 any animal owned or harbored primarily or in part for the purpose of fighting or any animal trained for fighting wild animals mean animals other than those defined as domestic including mammals birds reptiles and minimum space requirements for dog pens kennels and containment areas dog pens kennels and containment areas shall have minimum space sizes as determined below 1 dogs that weigh from one to 35 pounds shall be provided a minimum containment space of at least 80 square feet 2 dogs weighing from 36 to 75 pounds shall be contained in areas not less than 100 square feet 3 dogs weighing 76 or more pounds shall not be confined in areas of less than 120 square feet 4 additional space shall be provided for each additional dog contained in the same area and the minimum additional space needed for each additional dog shall be calculated by adding 50 percent of the minimum space required for the largest dog contained in the area 5 minimum space requirements apply to dog kennels fencedin and other containment areas in which dogs live e animal safety within dog kennels pens and containment areas dog kennels fencedin and other containment areas shall be adequately maintained to restrain the dogs as required by ordinances 9403 and 200514 as amended these areas shall be kept in such a manner as to be free of conditions that pose a threat to the dogs safety and health f protection from exposure to weather required dog kennels fencedin and other containment areas shall have adequate ventilation and shall provide clean dry shelter from inclement weather exposure to direct sun and exposure to extreme temperatures g cleanliness required dog kennels fencedin and other containment areas shall be kept humanely clean shall be free of excessive buildup of feces and shall have adequate supplies of fresh water and food food shall be controlled in a manner that will not promote the proliferation of rats vermin insects or other pests that pose a danger to the health of the dogs or of humans h reasonable dog medical treatment provided by owner dogs housed in kennels fencedin and other containment areas shall be kept reasonably free of injury and disease and shall be provided veterinarian care and treatment as required to maintain reasonably good health for all dogs within the restraint areas it shall be the responsibility of the dog owner to bear the costs of provisions of subsection 1037a constant restraint required if an animal is found at large not under restraint and its owner can be immediately identified and located such animal need not be impounded but may instead be released to the owner with a warning or citation issued at the time of release c if the owner of an impounded animal can be readily identified the animal control officer shall make reasonable attempts to locate the owner and inform him of the requirements for obtaining release of the animal d if after four days an animal that was found at large not under restraint is not redeemed by the owner and the owner is unknown the animal may be disposed of by using an approved humane method in all other cases the minimum holding period shall be seven days e if an animal has been hit by a vehicle or is suffering from another cause and it is deemed by a licensed veterinarian or an animal control officer or a city police officer to be beyond help the animal may be humanely destroyed without a period of confinement in such cases it shall be the responsibility of the animals owner to dispose of the animals carcass in a manner that meets state and federal health rules and regulations if the owner of the animal cannot be determined the city shall be responsible for properly disposing of the carcass f the animal control officer or any city police officer is empowered to issue a citation to the owner of any animal which is in violation of this article with first violation being $2500 second $5000 and third $10000 after third violation animal may be declared a nuisance released to the owner or guardian of the impounded animal a release fee of $2500 must be paid prior to the release h a currently unlicensed animal defined as an animal wearing one or both of its thereof or a licensed veterinarian for the vaccination the owner must then show proof of the vaccination to the rabies control officer the health officer or the city clerk if the animal has a current for a person to allow female dogs that are in their sexually receptive cycle of estrus commonly known as being in heat to go upon or have access to the streets roads or public areas within the city limits female dogs shall be confined in such places and in such a manner as will avoid nuisances being caused by the natural attraction of male dogs if the owner of a female dog has properly confined the female dog and male dogs are attracted to the female dog in estrus then the dogs that try to get to the female dog are not in proper restraint as required by this article and constitute a nuisance under such circumstances it is the responsibility of the owners of the male dog to confine their animal until the natural condition estrus in the female dog is over and the female dog no longer attracts male dogs a female dog in estrus is not properly confined by being on leash if a female dog in estrus is taken to public areas on a leash and males dogs are attracted to the female dog then the owner of the female dog is defined to have created a nuisance and may be issued a citation for being in violation of this article  2141994 rabies a any animal that has or is suspected of having rabies any animal which has bitten or exposed a human being or any animal that has been exposed to rabies shall be reported immediately to the police department the police department shall perform an investigation to determine if the animal is in conformance with this article and to determine if it has been inoculated within the required time periods upon investigation by the police department the findings of the investigation shall be reported by the police department to the person bitten andor to the attending physician within 24 hours of the time the animal bite was first reported to the police b the following actions shall be taken as well 1 quarantine generally a if a dog or cat is in conformance with all provisions of this article it shall be quarantined in a licensed veterinary clinic for observation for a period of ten days subsequent to the date of the exposure or as otherwise directed by the state health officer as required by state law the owner must pay boarding and observation fees to the clinic when the animal is released b if a dog or cat is not vaccinated for rabies and therefore is not in conformance with this article it shall be quarantined in a licensed veterinary clinic for a period of ten calendar days and must receive a rabies vaccination before being released board fees will be the responsibility of the victim if the owner is unknown c the quarantine requirement may be waived if the owner signs a euthanasia agreement agreement to have the animal humanely destroyed and pays the fees covering the euthanasia and the expenses of sending the animals head to the state health department laboratory for examination d if the animal is a canine corps dog or has been registered as a guard dog a guide dog or a hearing dog at the time the bite occurred and the animal was acting as a canine corps dog a guard dog a guide dog or a hearing dog when the bite occurred the owner shall report any relocations of the animal that occur within ten days of the bite to the city police department the owner shall also be required to confirm that the dog has received rabies vaccinations that were current at the time of the bite if such confirmation cannot be made then the dog shall be confined at a licensed veterinary clinic for observation for a period of ten calendar days from the time of the bite and the dog must receive a rabies vaccination before being released 2 animal suspected of rabies or exposed to rabies a if the dog or cat has been properly vaccinated for rabies it shall be quarantined for observation in a licensed veterinary clinic for a period of ten calendar days from the date the exposure was reported to the police department the animals owner is responsible for boarding and observation fees b if the dog or cat has bitten a human being is not licensed and the owner cannot be determined the animal shall be quarantined in a licensed veterinary clinic until it can be humanely destroyed c if the dog or cat is not properly vaccinated for rabies it shall be quarantined in a licensed veterinary clinic until it can be humanely destroyed the head of the animal suspected of rabies or exposure to rabies shall be submitted according to state and federal regulations for appropriate examination by the state health department laboratory 3 other animals a the period of quarantine for animals other than domesticated dogs and cats which have bitten or exposed a human being shall be determined by the state department of public health upon consultation with the us public health service  provided however that for those animal species where reliable epidemiologic data are lacking regarding duration of rabies virus secretion from the salivary glands such animals shall be humanely destroyed and the head submitted for rabies examination to the state health department laboratory b those domesticated species other than dogs and cats for which antirabies vaccine is recognized and recommended upon exposure or potential exposure to a known rabid animal shall be humanely destroyed or slaughtered immediately  provided however that the owner may have the option of quarantining such animals based on the recommendations of the state department of public health upon consultation with the us public health service 4 rabid animal a every animal confirmed to have rabies shall be committed to the care and quarantine of a licensed veterinary clinic and shall be disposed of in accordance with the laws of the state b information regarding an animal which has been confirmed to have rabies and which has bitten a human being shall be reported by the veterinarian who has custody of the rabid animal and to the attending physician of the person who was bitten  2141994 state law reference similar 7221985 enforcement it shall be unlawful for any person in the city to allow the house or building in which the people live or own or the premises around the house or the alley or street abutting the premises to become or remain in an unsanitary or unsightly condition a enforcement this provision shall be enforced by the city code enforcement officer who upon finding that this section is being violated shall issue written notification to the last party assessing the property for state taxes to the address on file in the tax office by certified or registered mail the mailing of the certified or registered mail notice properly addressed and postage prepaid shall constitute notice as required by this section in addition a copy of the notice is also posted at the property site the notice shall require the violation to be corrected within 14 days of the date of the notice the owner or person assessing the property for taxes shall have the right to file a written request for a hearing before the city council on this notice provided that the request is made in writing to the city clerk within 14 days of the notice this notice shall be required to set forth any objections to the finding by the city official b action if appeal is made if an appeal is made within the allotted time the city council shall hear the report together with any objections which may be raised by any owner whose property is liable to be assessed for the work and the council may make such modifications in the report as they deem necessary after which by resolution the report may be confirmed or denied if the report is confirmed the council shall allow the owner ten days to address the violation should the violation not be addressed within this time the council may authorize the code enforcement officer to abate the violation by cleaning the property and removing any trash or other violating condition from the property the code enforcement officer of the city shall coordinate an effort to go upon the property and address the abatement utilizing city services or contracting for the service after completion of this work the code enforcement officer shall render an itemized report to the council showing the cost incurred in abating the nuisance upon the filing of this cost a public hearing shall be held for consideration thereof with notice being given to the person assessing the property for taxes by first class mail at the public hearing if the council may approve the report of the code enforcement office and pass a resolution assessing a lien against the property for the recovery of the costs of abatement c action if no appeal is made if no request for hearing is made within the time required and the violation has not been corrected the code enforcement officer shall appear before the council and render his written report of the violation upon considering the report the council may find that the violation of the section exists and may authorize the code enforcement officer to abate the violation by cleaning the property and removing any trash or other violating condition from the property the code enforcement officer of the city shall coordinate an effort to go upon the property and address the abatement utilizing city services or contracting for the service after completion of this work the code enforcement officer shall render an itemized report to the council showing the cost incurred in abating the nuisance upon the filing of this cost a public hearing shall be held for consideration thereof with notice being given to the person assessing the property for taxes by first class mail at the public hearing if the council may approve the report of the code enforcement office and pass a resolution assessing a lien against the property for the recovery of the costs of abatement d lien assessment the amounts of the costs for the abating a violation of this section shall constitute special assessments against the land and as thus made and confirmed shall constitute a lien on the property for the amount of such assessment thereafter such amounts shall be collected at the same time and in the same manner as ordinary municipal assessments are collected and shall be subject to the same penalties a copy of the resolution shall also be filed in the office of the probate court of chambers county alabama imposing a lien on the property e criminal penalty the code enforcement officer or any law enforcement officer may issue a citation to the owner and occupant of the property upon which the violation exists requiring the person to appear in municipal or district court to answer charges for the violation of this section such citation shall name the party charged the address of the property where the alleged violation is located and the nature of the offense or violation it shall also apprise the person of the date time and place at which to appear in court such citation returnable to the municipal or district court shall be served on the owner of the property by any code enforcement officer for the city instead of placing a person under custodial arrest may issue a summons and complaint against a person charged with a violation of this section for purposes of this section the city authorizes the use of the uniform nontraffic citation and complaint form currently utilized by the city the procedure for issuing a citation is that when an arrest is to be made the arresting officer releases the person upon his written promise to appear in court at the designated time and place if the person refuses to sign the citation and appear in court the officer is to take the person into custody and bring him before any officer or official authorized to approve a bond f means of enforcement the code enforcement officer or any law enforcement officer may institute either or both enforcement procedures set forth above the institution of one procedure does not preclude the subsequent or simultaneous institution of the other procedure provided the criminal procedure is not used to collect any outstanding civil assessments against the subject property g penalties any said permit or if said permit is expired or been cancelled and the applicant has failed to secure a new permit to complete the work or if the applicant has violated any provisions of this article or of any permit issued or plan approved pursuant to this article and fails and refuses to cure such violation then the city shall have the right in addition to all other rights afforded to the city by law at the citys option to complete such work or to correct any defect or deficiency using the citys own forces or contractors hired for that purpose 2 the city shall have the right to draw on the surety bond provided by the applicant or demand payment directly from the applicant or the owner for the cost of such city work including without limitation legal fees and administrative expenses based either on costs and expenses incurred by the city or on the citys reasonable estimates of costs to be incurred 3 the city shall give the applicant written or oral notice of seven days and an opportunity to cure to the applicant before taking such action  provided however that no such notice and opportunity to cure shall be required in the event of repeated violations or in the event that a condition on or near the subject property poses in the determination of the building official a threat of any kind to the public or safety the applicant and the owner of the subject property shall be jointly and severally responsible for all costs and expenses incurred by the city including without limitation attorneys fees and administrative expenses in completing the demolition work   4142014  conduct of work upon the issuance of a permit for demolition of a building or structure the building or structure shall be promptly demolished or removed provided that all work done under the permit shall be subject to the supervision of the building official and to such reasonable restrictions as the building official may impose in regard to elements of safety and health it shall be unlawful for the applicant or property owner to demolish or remove a building or structure from the premises in such a manner that there remain holes or depressions dangerous to the public safety or that there shall remain debris or rubbish on the premises the applicant shall fill any existing holes left on the property level the property remove all debris and junk from the property and replant the property with appropriate vegetation within the time period designated by the building official the acceptance of areas designated to be seeded shall be based upon the building officials determination that the property ground preparation seeding etc has been accomplished and a satisfactory stand of grass has been established if a satisfactory stand of grass is not established the area shall be reseeded and mulched a satisfactory stand of grass is defined as a living and growing area of grass of not less than 100 percent ground coverage this may be deemed to include grass that is dormant during a cold or dry season but has roots which have taken hold in the soil and show sprouts that are capable of growing after the unfavorable period has passed the building official may permit the applicant or owner to retain the foundation if it is safe to do so and the applicant the owner or their agent either removes the foundation to a depth of 12 inches below grade or leaves an empty hard surface slab covering the foundation the applicant or owner shall immediately repair or cause to be repaired any damage to public rightsofway and utilities   4142014  penalty any person firm corporation assessed by a court of competent jurisdiction  2261996 secs 18411870  reserved article iii  tattoo establishments division 1  generally definitions the following words terms and phrases when used in this article shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning certificate of inspection means written approval from the health officer that a tattoo establishment has been inspected and meets all the terms of this article relating to physical facilities equipment and layout for operation of such business as well as any county or state regulations pertaining to the operation of such business operator means any individual firm company corporation or association that owns or operates an establishment where tattooing is performed and any individual who performs or practices the art of tattooing on the person of another tattoo tattooed tattooing means any method of placing indelible designs letters scrolls figures symbols or other marks upon or under the skin with dye ink pigment or any other substance resulting in the coloration of the skin by the aid of needles scalpels or any other instruments designed to touch or puncture the skin  9141992 cross reference definitions generally  12 health and sanitary requirements each person who operates a tattoo establishment shall comply with the following requirements 1 the room in which the tattooing is done shall have an area of not less than 100 square feet the walls floors and ceiling shall have an impervious smooth and washable surface 2 a toilet shall be located in the establishment and shall be accessible at all times that the tattoo establishment is open for business the lavatory shall be supplied with hot and cold running water soap and sanitary towels 3 all tables and other equipment shall be constructed of easily cleanable material shall be painted or finished in a light color with a smooth washable finish and shall be separated from waiting customers or observers by a panel at least six feet high or by a door 4 the entire premises and equipment shall be maintained in a clean sanitary condition and in good repair 5 the operator shall wash his hands thoroughly with antiseptic soap and water before starting to tattoo  the hands shall be dried with individual single use towels 6 no tattooing shall be done on any skin surface that has any rash pimples boils infections or manifests any evidence of unhealthy conditions 7 no skin area shall be penetrated abraded or treated with chemicals for the purpose of removing camouflaging or altering any blemish birthmark scar or tattoo 8 safety razors with a new singleservice blade for each customer or patron or a straight razor may be used and shall be thoroughly cleaned and sterilized before use on each customer or patron 9 the area to be tattooed shall first be thoroughly washed for a period of two minutes with warm water to which has been added an antiseptic liquid soap a sterile singleuse sponge shall be used to scrub the area after shaving and before tattooing is begun a solution of 70 percent alcohol shall be applied to the area with a singleuse sponge used and applied with a sterile instrument 10 only petroleum jelly in collapsible metal or plastic tubes or its equivalent as approved by the health officer shall be used on the area to be tattooed and it shall be applied with sterile gauze 11 the use of styptic pencils alum blocks or other solid styptics to check the flow of blood is strictly prohibited 12 inquiry shall be made and anyone giving a history of recent jaundice hepatitis hiv virus or any other communicable disease may not be tattooed 13 singleservice or individual containers of dye or ink shall be used for each patron and the container therefor shall be discarded immediately after completing work on a patron and any dye in which the needles were dipped shall not be used on another person excess dye or ink shall be removed from the skin with an individual sterile sponge or a disposable paper tissue which shall be used only on one person and then the tattooed area shall be washed with sterile gauze saturated with an antiseptic soap solution approved by the health officer or a 70 percent alcohol solution the tattooed area shall be allowed to dry and petroleum jelly from a collapsible or plastic tube shall be applied using sterile gauze a sterile gauze dressing shall then be fastened to the tattooed area with adhesive  9141992 care of instruments a storing of instruments all clean and readytouse needles and instruments shall be kept in a closed glass or metal case or storage cabinet while not in use such cabinet shall be maintained in a sanitary manner at all times b sterilizing of instruments a steam sterilizer autoclave shall be provided for sterilizing all needles and similar instruments before use on any customer person or patron alternate sterilizing procedures may only be used when specifically approved by the health officer sterilization of equipment will be accomplished by exposure to live steam for at least 30 minutes at a minimum pressure of 15 pounds per square inch temperature of 240 degrees fahrenheit or 116 degrees celsius c use of instruments the needles and instruments required to be sterilized shall be so used handled and temporarily placed during tattooing so that they will not be contaminated  9141992 recordkeeping permanent records for each patron or customer shall be maintained by the licensee or operator of the establishment before the tattooing operation begins the patron or customer shall be required personally to enter on a record form provided for such establishments the date his name address date of birth social security number security number if a member of the armed forces place of employment and his signature such records shall be maintained in the tattoo establishment and shall be available for inspection by the health officer records shall be retained by the operator or licensee for a period of not less than five years in the event of a change of ownership or closing of the business all such records shall be made available to the health officer  9141992 infections no person customer or patron having any skin infection or other disease of the skin or any communicable disease shall be tattooed all infections resulting from the practice of tattooing which become known to the operator shall promptly be reported to the health officer by the person owning or operating the tattoo establishment and the infected client shall be referred to a physician  9141992 pigments and dyes all pigments dyes inks colors etc used in tattooing shall be sterile and free from bacteria virus particles and noxious agents or substances and the pigments dyes and colors used from stock solutions for each customer or patron shall be placed in a singleservice receptacle and such receptacle and remaining solution shall be discarded after use on each customer or patron  9141992 bandages and surgical dressings all bandages and surgical dressings used in connection with the tattooing of a person shall be sterile  9141992 inspections at reasonable times the health officer may conduct periodic inspections of any tattoo establishment for the purpose of determining whether or not the establishment and the persons performing the art of tattooing therein are in compliance with all applicable health provisions of this article as well as any other city county or state provisions it shall be unlawful for any person or operator of a tattoo establishment willfully to prevent or restrain the health officer from entering any licensed establishment where tattooing is being performed for the purpose of inspecting the premises after proper identification is presented to the operator  9141992 penalty for violation of article in addition to the revocation and suspension of any license any person violating any provision of this article shall be punished as provided in section 111 for each offense  9141992 secs 188018100  reserved division 2  license required it shall be unlawful for any person to engage in the business of terms and phrases when used in this article shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning cigarette means a roll of finely cut tobacco or any substitutes therefor enclosed in paper prepared for smoking by individuals in addition to the definition of cigarettes found in cigarettes shall also include cigarillos which are sold in packages cigarillos sold in packages shall be taxed as cigarettes and not as cigars dealer means any wholesale dealer or retail dealer as defined in this section package means the individual box or other container from which or in which retail sales of tobacco products mentioned in this section are normally made or intended to be made retail dealer means any person firm or other entity other than a wholesale dealer who sells or delivers tobacco products within the city or the police jurisdiction of the city and any person firm or entity operating under a retail dealers license retail price means the retail selling price of the tobacco products before adding the amount of the tax assessed in this article or any tobacco tax assessed by the state sold and sale mean any transfer of title or possession or both exchange or barter conditional or otherwise in any manner or by any means whatsoever for a consideration or any agreement therefor including rewards prizes or premiums of tobacco products given as a result of operations on punch boards shooting galleries or other activities stamps means the stamp or stamps by the use of which the taxes levied on cigarettes under this article are paid store and stored mean the storage or warehousing of tobacco products in any manner or the withdrawal or use of the same for any purpose other than for resale or reshipment outside the city tobacco products means cigarettes cigars chewing tobacco smoking tobacco snuff or any substitute of these products wholesale dealer means a person who sells or delivers within the city or its police jurisdiction at wholesale only tobacco products to retail dealers for the purpose of resale only  4271992   9242001 cross reference definitions generally  12 construction of article a this article shall not be construed to tax interstate commerce or any business of the united states government or any branch or agency b this article shall not be construed to apply to tobacco products stored for the purpose of resale or reshipment outside the city and its police jurisdiction and which are actually so resold or reshipped c this article shall not be construed to repeal any of the provisions of the general license provisions of the city but shall be held to be cumulative d whenever the requisite amount of stamps has been affixed to cigarettes and whenever the tax levied in this article on other tobacco products has been paid this article shall not be construed to require additional stamps or additional tax  4271992 levy of tax in city in addition to all taxes now imposed by containing 20 cigarettes or cigarillos small cigars or less when cigarettes or cigarillos are packaged in cartons this tax is for each package within the carton 2 cigars including cheroots and stogies such a manner as to be suitable for chewing only and not suitable for smoking so sold stored or delivered 4 smoking tobacco a license tax in the sum of $012 for each package of smoking tobacco including granulated plug cut crimp cut ready rubbed and other kinds and forms of tobacco prepared in such a manner as to be suitable for smoking in a pipe or cigarette so sold stored or delivered 5 products in the police jurisdiction of the city in an amount equal to onehalf of the amount levied for the sale storage or delivery of tobacco products in the corporate limits of the city  4271992 stamps sold by city clerk  inscription  sale to wholesalers and others the city clerk shall keep on hand for sale an adequate quantity of stamps to be affixed to each package of cigarettes in the denominations as required under this article each stamp shall have inscribed thereon the words city of valley  tobacco tax but such words need not be arranged in the foregoing order and may be abbreviated such stamps may be sold to wholesale dealers only by the city clerk at a price equal to 90 percent of the full amount the remaining ten percent of such full amount representing compensation to the wholesale dealer for the labor of affixing such stamps to the packages in which the cigarettes are contained such ten percent compensation to be allowed to such wholesale dealer shall apply only to purchases of stamps having a face value of not less than $20000 all other persons except wholesale dealers must pay the full face amount of the stamps but no person shall be entitled to purchase any such number of stamps as shall cause the purchase price to include a fraction of a cent  4271992 affixing stamps before any cigarettes shall be sold stored or delivered within the corporate limits of the city or within its police jurisdiction by any person such person shall affix or cause to be affixed to each package of cigarettes a stamp obtained from the city clerk in the amounts set out in this article in payment of the license taxes imposed by this article every person shall within one hour after receipt of any cigarettes within the city or within the police jurisdiction of the city unless sooner offered for sale cause stamps of the requisite amount of taxes to be affixed as provided in this section and shall cause the stamps to be canceled by writing or stamping with waterproof ink across the face of each stamp such registered number as shall be furnished to such person by the city clerk after such stamping has been begun it shall be continued with reasonable diligence by such person until all unstamped cigarettes shall have been stamped and the stamps canceled as provided in this section but no stamps required to be affixed to any package of cigarettes shall after the stamps have been affixed as provided in this section be again used in payment of any part of the tax levied under this article in the case of cigarettes sold by retail in packages the stamps shall be affixed to each individual package in such a way that such stamps shall be torn in two or mutilated when such package is opened  4271992 records and reports of dealers  reports of violations every wholesale dealer shall at the time of selling or delivering tobacco products into the city or its police jurisdiction make a true duplicate invoice of the sale or delivery which shall show full and complete details of the sale or delivery of such tobacco products every wholesale and every retail dealer shall keep a record of the purchase sale exchange or receipt of tobacco products all such invoices and records and all canceled checks and memoranda pertaining to any such purchase sale exchange or receipt of tobacco products shall be retained for a period of 18 months and shall be subject to inspection by an agent of the city who shall have the power and authority to enter upon the premises of any dealer at all reasonable times for the purpose of examining such invoices records canceled checks or other memoranda any person who purchases or receives in any manner whatsoever tobacco products which does not have stamps affixed in the manner required by this article shall within three days after receipt of such tobacco products report the receipt and purchase to the city clerk giving the date of purchase or receipt the name of the person from whom purchased or received and a list describing the tobacco products so purchased or received such report must be made by registered or certified mail or in person  4271992 taxes due and payable date the tax levied under the provisions of this article on all tobacco products with the exception of cigarettes shall be due and payable in monthly installments on or before the 20th day of each month next succeeding the month in which the tax accrued on or before the 20th day of each month every wholesale dealer in tobacco products shall file with the city clerk a true and correct monthly statement in writing of all tobacco products except cigarettes sold or delivered during the preceding months for which he is or shall be liable for the payment of the license tax and shall in each and every instance upon the filing of a statement furnish to the clerk such additional information either oral or in writing as the clerk may require as to the sale or delivery of any tobacco products covered by such statement and shall at the time of making such statement pay to the city clerk for the city the amount of the license tax for the preceding month covered by such statement  4271992 prohibited acts among others the following acts and omissions shall be unlawful 1 it shall be unlawful for any person who is required by this article to affix stamps to cigarettes to fail to affix such stamps or to cancel such stamps in the manner or within the time required by this article 2 it shall be unlawful for any person to sell offer for sale store or deliver within the city or within its police jurisdiction any cigarettes where stamps have not been affixed and canceled as provided in this article 3 it shall be unlawful for any person to have in his possession or under his control any cigarettes where stamps have not been affixed in the manner as required by this article for more than six hours after receipt of such cigarettes on the premises of such person the possession of each package of cigarettes not having proper stamps affixed as required by this article shall be deemed a separate offense 4 it shall be unlawful to manufacture buy sell offer for sale or possess or to attempt so to do any reproduction or counterfeit of the stamps provided for in this article or to possess tools implements instruments or materials of any kind necessary or appropriate to reproduce or counterfeit such stamps or to alter or cause to be altered any stamps provided for in this section 5 it shall be unlawful to remove from a package or otherwise prepare any stamp with intent to use or cause the same to be used after it has already been used or to buy sell offer for sale or give away any washed removed altered or restored stamp to any person or to have in possession any such washed or restored or altered stamp or for the purpose of indicating payment of any tax under this article to reuse any stamp which has theretofore been used for the payment of any tax provided in this article or to sell any stamp provided for herein except as to sales made by the city clerk 6 it shall be unlawful to reuse or refill with cigarettes any package from which cigarettes have been removed and with respect to which the tax has theretofore been paid 7 it shall be unlawful for any person who is in this article required to keep records to fail or omit to keep the records in the manner provided in this article or to refuse to permit the agent of the city to inspect the records at any reasonable hour or to interfere with or obstruct the agent of the city in the making of any such inspection 8 it shall be unlawful for any person who is herein required to file statements with the city clerk to fail or omit to make or file any statement provided in this section within the time specified in this section or to make any false statement therein and any such offense shall be a continuing offense against the city and each day during which such person shall sell or deliver tobacco products in the city or police jurisdiction during such default shall constitute a separate offense 9 it shall be unlawful for any person who is required to pay the license tax provided for in this article to fail or omit to pay the tax within the time specified in this article and such offense shall be a continuing offense against the city and each day during which such person shall sell store or deliver tobacco products in the city or its police jurisdiction during such default shall constitute a separate offense  4271992 inspection of machines the city inspector is hereby authorized to city of valley cemetery committee and the city treasurer shall be the treasurer of the city of valley cemetery committee b the city of valley cemetery committee is authorized to receive personal property including but not limited to money bonds stocks checks certificates of deposit and real property these donations may be held invested banked andor sold donations may be received from individuals estates trusts corporations partnerships associations andor any and all government bodies and agents all donations shall be placed in the city of valley cemetery fund donations of all types may be sold invested or otherwise expended at the discretion of the city of valley cemetery committee provided that all proceeds are deposited into the city of valley cemetery fund c the city of maintain information on the owners of burial plots a list of names of person buried in the cemeteries may be published for genealogical research and reference d the city of valley cemetery committee the administration of the city of valley cemetery fund and to the administration of the cemeteries specified by this article e the city of valley cemetery committee shall adopt such rules and procedures of conduct as it deems necessary provided that such bylaws rules and procedures are consistent with the stated purposes and provisions of this article and do not violate state or federal laws  9251995 city of valley cemetery fund a the city of valley cemetery fund shall be independent of all other city accounts and funds and shall be dedicated to those activities specified within this cemetery fund c the city of valley cemetery fund may be spent for surveying plots creating and updating cemetery maps locating boundaries and burial sites preparing long range plans hiring consultants independent cemetery associations prior to this date or specified within burial lot deeds issued prior to this date remain in effect and are grandfathered aside from these exceptions these rules and regulations apply equally to all city cemetery users i general 1 the cemeteries will be open to visitors during the day but no visitors will be allowed after sunset or before sunrise children under 13 years of age must be accompanied by a responsible adult 2 the speed limit on cemetery roads is five miles per hour no parking will be allowed off paved or designated roads 3 the city of valley shall be notified at least 24 hours in advance of the day and time of a burial to verify lot ownership and approve the burial location the city of valley shall be given all pertinent information regarding the deceased and the responsible survivors prior to burial 4 flower receptacles shall be plastic masonry bronze or pottery glass wood paper and corrodible metal containers may not be used as flower receptacles flower receptacles should be placed next to the monument or grave marker not on the grass 5 should lot owners desire to sell their unused lots they must sell it to the city of valley for the original purchase price a lot may be transferred from one family member to another by notifying and obtaining approval of the city of valley this change must be shown on the original deed or a new deed shall be required cost for changing or creating new deeds must be paid by the lot owner requesting the change 6 games recreational activities and social gatherings not associated with burials memorial services or grave visitations are prohibited unless specifically approved by the city of valley ii interments and disinterments 1 all interments shall be enclosed in a regular concrete or metal vault vaults of other constructions must be approved in writing by the city of valley burial vaults shall be covered by at least 18 inches of soil 2 no interment will be permitted in a grave space that has not been fully paid for 3 no burial will be permitted unless a permit has been issued by the city of valley 4 no disinterment will be allowed until proper authority is given 5 a cemetery lot is to be used only as a burial lot for human remains 6 the city of valley shall not be held responsible for interments in the wrong cemetery lot for cases in which the city of valley was not involved in the location of the lot iii monuments and markers 1 all monument dealers and grave diggers operating within the city of valley shall be licensed by the city of valley 2 all monument dealers and grave diggers operating within city cemeteries will be responsible for damage they may cause to cemetery property markers andor monuments 3 the city of valley shall not be held responsible for scratches or marks on privately owned grave markers or monuments that may have occurred during normal maintenance or as a result of natural deterioration 4 headstones and ground level flat bronze markers will be permitted in all city owned cemeteries 5 headstones shall not exceed three feet six inches in height above the ground 6 each grave shall be properly marked within twelve months following burial with a headstone or flat marker made from granite marble or bronze iv maintenance 1 the city of valley shall be responsible for maintenance and upkeep of its officially designated city cemeteries 2 lot owners may maintain their own lots provided they adhere to the following city cemetery rules a ground levels must not be altered b grass must be cut on schedule coinciding with the citys cutting schedule c no mounds will be allowed over graves beyond three months from the burial date d no walls shall be built on or around burial lots e no shrubbery trees or flowers shall be planted on the lots f one single bench or seat made of marble granite or concrete may be placed on a family lot g no signs banners flags or decorations other than floral and american flags not exceeding 18 inches in height shall be placed on lots unless the city of valley has proclaimed a special memorial occasion for which special decorations may be used on a temporary basis v sexton the duties and responsibilities of the city cemetery sexton shall include the following 1 furnish information to the city concerning sale of burial lots and any other information relating to record keeping 2 be available to show prospective burial lot buyers location of lots for sale 3 be available to assist family members and funeral directors in locating burial lots 4 monitor the condition of i  generally purpose in order to ensure that the residents of the city of valley continue to receive quality care rendered by emergency medical service providers emsp to ensure quality control over the emsp and to facilitate the prompt and coordinated dispatch of emergency transport units when needed to protect life safety and health and to further prompt the health safety and welfare of its citizens it is hereby declared that the city of valley alabama designates the city of valley alabama ems service as the medical service for all emergency and nonemergency calls within the city limits and the ems service area pursuant to the procedures hereinafter stated additionally the city ems director will determine if the patient is to be transported by a private ambulance provider or by city ems transport vehicle the rules and regulations of private ambulances and municipal emergency and nonemergency transport vehicles in the city as set out herein are hereby established by the city council exercising sound legislative judgment  art 1 1252016 definitions the following words terms and phrases when used in this article shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section except operation of an ambulance within the city shall be in writing signed to and sworn by the applicant and shall be filed with the ems director of the city or his duly authorized representative this application shall be on a form prescribed by the ems director and shall contain at least the following a the name and address of the applicant and the trade name under which the applicant does or color scheme of each vehicle c whether or not the applicant has ever been convicted of any crimes directly or indirectly related to the duties and responsibilities of operating ambulances d whether or not the applicant his associates or employees have any claims or judgment against them for damages resulting from the negligent operation of any ambulance or any other vehicle e the nature and character of the service that the applicant proposes to render  then facts showing the demand for such service the experience that the applicant has had in rendering such service and the period of time if any that he has rendered it in the city or other jurisdictions f documentation from the applicants insurance carrier stating that the insurance required hereunder is available to the applicant and that such coverage is or will be provided prior to the issuance by the ems director of the permit to operate hereunder in this regard such applicant shall be required to have in full force and effect an automobile liability insurance policy covering such ambulance providing coverage of not less than $100000000 for injury or damage to any one person and $100000000 for injury or damage to any number of persons arising out of any one accident resulting from the operation of such ambulance or ambulances  art 4 1252016 investigation of application upon receipt of a properly filed application
