commission shall compile and collect information and conduct surveys of historic resources within the city after compiling and collecting this information the commission shall present to the city council recommendations for historic districts and properties  provided however that prior to the commissions recommendation of a historic district or historic property to the city council for designation the commission shall prepare a report consisting of 1 a physical description  2 a statement of the historical cultural architectural andor aesthetic significance  3 a map showing district boundaries and classification ie historic nonhistoric intrusive of individual properties therein and showing boundaries of individual historic properties  4 a statement justifying district or individual property boundaries  and 5 representative photographs b designation of a historic district 1 criteria for selection of historic districts a historic district is a geographically definable area which contains buildings structures sites objects landscape features and works or art or a combination which a represents one or more periods styles or types of architecture typical of one or more eras in the history of the municipality county state or region  b represents a significant aspect of the cultural political economic military or social history of the locality region state or nation  c has had a significant relationship with the life of a historic person or event representing a major aspect of the history of the locality region state or nation  d is a part of the historic architectural archaeological or aesthetic heritage of the locality region state or nation  e contains vernacular structures which contribute to an overall character and sense of place which is representative of the city 2 boundaries of a historic district boundaries of a historic district shall be shown on the official zoning map or other map of the city which is designated as a public record 3 evaluation of properties within historic districts individual properties within historic districts shall be classified as a historic contributes to the district  b nonhistoric does not contribute but does not detract from the district  c intrusive detracts from the district c designation of a historic property 1 criteria for selection of historic properties a historic property is a building structure site object work of art including the adjacent area necessary for its proper appreciation or use deemed worthy of preservation by reason of value to the city for one of the following reasons a it is an outstanding example of a structure representative of its era b it is one of the few remaining examples of past architectural style c it is a place or structure associated with an event or persons of historic or cultural significance to the city state or the region d it is a site of natural or aesthetic interest that is continuing to contribute to the cultural or historical development and heritage of the city county state or region e the building or structure is an example of an architectural style or combination of architectural styles which is representative of the city or which is unique to the city 2 boundary description boundaries shall be shown on the map of the city which is designated as a public record d requirements for adopting an ordinance for the designation of historic districts and historic properties 1 application for designation of historic districts or property designations may be proposed by the city council the commission or a historical society neighborhood association or group of property owners may apply to the commission for designation 2 required components of a designation ordinance any ordinance designating any property or district as historic shall a list each property in a proposed historic district or describe the proposed individual historic property  b set forth the names of the owners of the designated properties  c require that a certificate of appropriateness be obtained from the commission prior to any material change in appearance of the designated property  and d require that the property or district be shown on the map of the city and kept as a public record to provide notice of such designation 3 required public hearings the commission shall hold a public hearing on any proposed article for the designation of any historic district or property notice of the hearing shall be published in at least three consecutive issues in the principal newspaper of the local circulation and written notice of the hearing shall be mailed by the commission to all owners and occupants of such properties all such notices shall be published or mailed not less than ten nor more than 20 days prior to the date set for the public hearing a notice sent by ordinary mail to the last known owner of the property shown on the county tax records and a notice sent by ordinary mail to the address of the property to the attention of the occupant shall constitute legal notice to the owner and occupant under this article 4 recommendations on proposed designations a recommendation to affirm modify or withdraw the proposed ordinance for designation shall be made by the commission within 15 days following the public hearing and shall be in the form of a resolution to the city council 5 city council action on commission recommendation following receipt of the commissions recommendation the city council may adopt the ordinance as proposed may adopt the ordinance with any amendments it deems necessary or may reject the ordinance 6 notification of adoption of ordinance for designation within 30 days following the adoption of the ordinance for designation by the city council the owners and occupants of each designated historic property and the owners and occupants of each structure site or work of art located within a designated historic district shall be given written notification of such designation by the commission which notice shall apprise the owners and occupants of the necessity of obtaining a certificate of appropriateness prior to the undertaking any material change in appearance of the historic property designated or within the historic district designated a notice sent by ordinary mail to the last known owner of the property of the property shown on the county tax records and a notice sent by ordinary mail to the address of the property to the attention of the occupant shall constitute legal notice to the owner and occupant under this article 7 notification of other agencies regarding designation the commission shall notify all municipal agencies within the city of the ordinance for designation 8 moratorium on applications for alteration or demolition while ordinance for designation is pending if an ordinance for designation is being considered the commission shall have the authority to freeze the status of the involved property a  4 9141992 application to city of valley historic preservation commission for certificate of appropriateness a approval of alterations demolitions or new construction in historic districts or involving historic properties after the designation by ordinance of a historic property or of a historic district no historic property may be demolished no building or structure in a historic district may be erected or demolished and no material change in the exterior appearance of such historic property or of a structure site object or work of art within such historic district shall be made or be permitted to be made by the owner or occupant unless or until the application for a certificate of appropriateness has been submitted to and approved by the commission b approval of new construction within designated districts the commission shall issue certificates of appropriateness to new structures constructed within designated historic districts if these structures conform in design scale building materials setback and landscaping to the character of the district specified in the design criteria developed by the commission c approval of signs within designated districts signs shall be considered as structures and no sign on a historic property or in a historic district shall be changed erected or demolished unless and until a certificate of appropriateness is approved by the commission d approval of alterations or demolitions of public property within historic districts or public property which has been designated as a historic property the requirement of a certificate of appropriateness shall apply to public property which has been designated as a historic property or which is contained in a historic district and shall apply to all actions by public authorities which involve historic properties and properties within historic districts e approval of painting originally unpainted surfaces the painting of originally unpainted surfaces shall require a certificate of appropriateness f interior alterations in its review of applications for certificates of appropriateness the commission shall not consider interior arrangement or use having no effect on exterior architectural features g failure to maintain a historic property demolition by neglect and the failure to maintain a historic property or a structure in a historic district shall constitute a change for which a certificate of appropriateness is necessary h guidelines and criteria for certificates of appropriateness the commission shall adopt rules and regulations setting forth the procedure for submission and consideration of applications for certificates of appropriateness the commission shall also adopt general design standards which shall apply in considering the granting and denial of certificates of appropriateness design standards shall be in compliance with the secretary of the interiors standards for historic preservation projects including the secretarys standard for rehabilitation i submission of plans to commission an application for a certificate of appropriateness shall be accompanied by such drawings photographs plans or other documentation as may be required by the commission applications involving demolition or relocation shall be accompanied by the postdemolition or relocation plans for the site j acceptable commission reaction to applications for certificate of appropriateness 1 the commission shall approve the application and issue a certificate of appropriateness if it finds that the proposed material change in appearance would not have a substantial adverse effect on the aesthetic historic or architectural significance and value of the historic property or the historic district in making this determination the commission shall consider in addition to any other pertinent factors the historical and architectural value and significance architectural style general design arrangement texture and material of the architectural features involved and their relationship to the exterior architectural style and pertinent features of the other structures in the immediate neighborhood 2 the commission shall deny a certificate of appropriateness if it finds that the proposed material change in appearance would have substantial adverse effects on the aesthetic historic or architectural significance and value of the historic property or the historic district the commission shall not grant certificates of appropriateness for demolition or relocation without reviewing at the same time the postdemolition or postrelocation plans for the site k public meetings and hearings on applications for certificates of appropriateness  notices and right to be heard applications for certificates of appropriateness shall be considered by the commission at public meetings held at publicly accessible locations and times as may be designated and publicly announced by the commission or one of its officers at least seven days prior to the review of a certificate of appropriateness the commission shall take such action as may reasonably be required to inform the owners of any property likely to be affected by reason of the application and shall give any applicant and such owners an opportunity to be heard in cases where the commission deems it necessary it may hold a public hearing concerning the application l deadline for approval or rejection of application for certificate of appropriateness 1 the commission shall approve or reject an application for a certificate of appropriateness within 45 days after the filing by the owner or occupant of a historic property or of a historic structure site object of work of art located within a historic district evidence of approval shall be by certificate of appropriateness issued by the commission notice of the issuance or denial of a certificate of appropriateness shall be sent by ordinary mail to the applicant and all other persons who have requested such notice in writing filed with the commission 2 failure of the commission to act within 45 days shall constitute approval and no other evidence of approval shall be needed m necessary actions to be taken by commission upon rejection of application for certificate of appropriateness 1 if the commission rejects an application it shall state its reasons for doing so and shall transmit a record of such actions and reasons in writing to the applicant the commission may suggest alternative courses of action it thinks proper if it disapproves of the application submitted the applicant if he so desires may make modifications to the plans and may resubmit the application at any time after doing so 2 in cases where the application covers a material change in the appearance of a structure which would require the issuance of a building permit the rejection of the application for a certificate of appropriateness by the commission shall be binding upon the building official or other administrative officer charged with issuing building permits and in such cases no building permit shall be issued n appeals any person having a request for a certificate of appropriateness denied by the commission or architectural review board as provided in section 4244 may appeal such denial to the county circuit court o recording of applications for certificate of appropriateness the commission shall keep a public record of all applications for certificates of appropriateness and of all the commissions proceedings in connection with the application p requirements of conformance with certificate of appropriateness 1 all work performed pursuant to an issued certificate of appropriateness shall conform to the requirements of such certificate if work is performed not in accordance with such certificate the commission shall issue a cease and desist order and all work shall cease 2 the city council or the commission shall be authorized to institute any appropriate action or proceeding in a court of competent jurisdiction to prevent any material change in appearance of a designated historic property or historic district except those changes made in compliance with the provisions of this article or to prevent any illegal act or conduct with respect to such historic property or historic district q certificate of appropriateness void if construction not commenced a certificate of appropriateness shall become void unless construction is commenced within six months of the date of issuance certificates of appropriateness shall be issued for a period of 18 months and are renewable r technical advice the commission shall have the power to seek technical advice from outside its members on any application a  5 9141992   maintenance of historic properties a expedited review procedures for approval of routine maintenance the commission may adopt expedited review procedures for approval of routine maintenance to historic properties or to buildings or structures in historic districts routine maintenance to historic properties includes ordinary maintenance or repair of any exterior architectural or environmental feature in or on a historic property to correct deterioration decay or damage or to sustain the existing form that does not involve a material change in design material or outer appearance expedited review procedures shall waive the requirements for submission of an application for a certificate of appropriateness and for consideration at a public meeting b failure to provide ordinary maintenance or repair property owners of historic properties or properties within historic districts shall not allow their buildings to deteriorate by failing to provide ordinary maintenance or repair the commission shall be charged with the following responsibilities regarding deterioration by neglect 1 the commission shall monitor the condition of historic properties and existing buildings in historic districts to determine if they are being allowed to deteriorate by neglect such conditions as broken windows doors and openings which allow the elements and vermin to enter the deterioration of exterior architectural features or the deterioration of a buildings structural system shall constitute failure to provide ordinary maintenance or repair 2 if the commission determines a failure to provide ordinary maintenance or repair the commission will notify the owner of the property and set forth the steps which need to be taken to remedy the situation the owner of such property will have 30 days in which to do this 3 if the condition is not met in 30 days the owner shall be punished as provided in section 4246 and at the direction of the city council the commission may perform such maintenance or repair as is necessary to prevent deterioration by neglect the owner of the property shall be liable for the cost of such maintenance and repair performed by the commission a  6 9141992 phrases when used in this article shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning captured personal property means any personal property as defined in ala 197  1118 taken into the custody of a police officer in his official capacity for use as evidence or as lost stolen or abandoned property or otherwise  4141986 cross reference definitions generally  12 creation of office of custodian of property the office of custodian of property is created the custodian shall be the duly appointed or acting chief of police  4141986 receiving  numbering  security it shall be the duty of every police officer to deliver promptly to the custodian of property all captured personal property including money which he may take into his custody and it shall be the duty of the custodian of property to receive such property upon delivery by a police officer to the custodian of property of any captured personal property the custodian shall execute in duplicate a receipt for such property upon a form approved by the city clerk describing the property as accurately as possible which receipt shall be numbered and the duplicate retained by such custodian and the original turned over to such police officer the custodian of property shall attach to such property so received a tag bearing a number corresponding to the number placed on the receipt issued the custodian of property shall keep such property safely in a room provided by the city or other secure location under the control of the city unless the property is money and in that event the money shall be deposited in a bank account to the credit of the city identified as captured personal property he shall keep such room or other location locked or otherwise secured and no person other than the custodian shall have access thereto unless accompanied by the custodian the custodian shall maintain and keep in his office a permanent record showing the date of the taking of each piece of such property the place where found and taken and a description of the property  4141986 delivery to rightful owner a any captured personal property other than property being held as evidence in any legal proceeding pending or contemplated and other than property subject to condemnation or forfeiture under the laws of the state or under the provisions of other ordinances of the city shall become subject to demand of the rightful owner for its return upon the date of receipt by the custodian of property any captured personal property being held as evidence in any legal proceeding pending or contemplated other than property subject to condemnation or forfeiture under the laws of the state or under the provisions of other ordinances of the city shall become subject to demand of the rightful owner for its return upon the date of final termination of such legal proceeding b the custodian of property shall deliver any property received by him as such custodian of property to the rightful owner upon demand made after such property has become subject to demand therefor within the terms of this article and before its sale as provided in this article and upon payment by rightful owner of reasonable expenses of taking the property in charge its maintenance and storage and the cost of publication c upon delivery by the custodian of property to an owner of any captured personal property the custodian of property at the time of making such delivery shall take the receipt of such owner for the property so delivered upon the duplicate receipt of the custodian for such property or upon a paper annexed to such duplicate receipt such receipt of the owner shall show the day on which such delivery was made the name and address of the person to whom such property was delivered a brief description of the property delivered and a number corresponding to the number of the original receipt of the custodian covering such property  4141986 sale  generally on june 30 and december 31 of each year any personal property other than property being held as evidence in any legal proceeding pending or contemplated or subject to condemnation or forfeiture under the state law or under the provisions of other ordinance provisions of the city which shall have been taken up and stored and shall have remained in the custody of the custodian for a period of three months or more shall be sold by the city purchasing agent at the direction of the chief of police at public auction to the highest bidder for cash such sales to be made after notice of the time and place shall have first been given by publication of notice once a week for two successive weeks in a newspaper published or of general circulation in the city the first publication shall be at least 20 days before the sale the owner of any of the property taken up and stored may redeem the property at any time prior to its sale under the provisions of section 4674b each article shall be sold separately and a notation in the storage record book shall be made of the amount received for each article the person making the sale shall have the right to reject any and all bids if the amount bid is unreasonably low and shall have the right to continue the sales from time to time if no bidders are present if no bids are received or the bid is rejected as being unreasonably low or the city desires to purchase the article then the purchasing agent of the city shall be permitted to bid a reasonable amount on behalf of the city and the property shall then be sold to the city if its bid is the highest  provided however that the purchasing agent shall make no single purchase on behalf of the city under this article where the purchase price amounts to $100000 or more notwithstanding the provisions of other resolutions or ordinances of the city the proceeds of the sale shall be paid into the general fund of the city after deducting and paying all expenses incurred in the taking up maintaining and selling of the property where the captured personal property is money no sale or publication shall be required and if the money has not been claimed by the rightful owner on june 30 and december 31 of each year all money having been held for a period of three months as captured personal property in an account as provided in section 4673 shall be paid into the general fund of the city after deducting expenses in connection therewith  4141986 perishable property in all cases of perishable property it shall be the duty of the police officer who captures such property to report the property with all convenient speed to the custodian of property who shall have the power in his discretion to order such property disposed of at public or private sale and the proceeds of such sale shall become captured personal property and shall be treated the same as money is treated in sections 4673 and 4675 with the expenses of sale of such perishable property being deducted from the money upon delivery to its rightful owner  4141986 secs 467746110  reserved article iv  reserve police officers footnotes  2  cross reference officers and employees manufacturers specifications for the capabilities and capacities of the tow trucks and all towing equipments any trucks andor towing equipment meeting the requirements of the department prior to  shall be deemed adequate for use up to  any trucks andor towing equipment acquired after  must meet the capacities and specifications set forth in these regulations each tow truck shall be equipped with only those winches and cranes that have been produced and constructed by a manufacturer of such equipment who carries product liability and which regularly produces winches and cranes a wrecker classifications 1 class a light duty wrecker class a wreckers for towing vehicles weighing 7000 pounds or less passengers cars pickup trucks motorcycles small trailers and similar vehicles shall meet the following minimum requirements a conventional wrecker 1 minimum gross vehicle weight rating gvwr of not less than 10000pounds 2 individual boom capacity of not less than 8000 pounds as rated by the manufacturer 3 individual pto or hydraulic power winch capacity of not less than 8000 pounds as rated by the manufacturer with at least 100 feet of threeeighthinch cable drum 4 a manufactured wheellift with a retracting lifting capacity of not less than 3500 pounds as rated by the manufacturer with safety chains 5 dual rear wheels 6 additional safety equipment as specified by the regulations b rollback wrecker 1 minimum gross vehicle weight rating gvwr of not less than 11000 pounds 2 must have at least an 8000 pound of winch as rated by the manufacturer with at least 50 feet of threeeighthsinch cable or larger 3 comealongs chains or other similar devices shall not be used as substitutes for winch and cable 4 a brake lock device 5 additional safety equipment as specified by the regulations 2 class b medium duty wrecker class b wreckers for towing vehicles weighing between 7001 and 1700 pounds or multiple vehicles weighing 7000 pounds respectively mediumsized trucks road tractorstrailers and similar vehicles shall meet the following requirements a the tow truck chassis shall have a minimum gross vehicle weight rating gvwr of not less than 22000 pounds b must have at least a 12ton boom assembly as rated by the manufacturer c two winches each of 10000 pound capacity or more as rated by the manufacturer d a manufactured wheellift with a retracting lifting capacity of not less than 6500 pounds as rated by the manufacturer with safety chains e comealongs chains or other similar devices shall not be used as substitutes for winch and cable f additional safety equipment as specified by the regulations 3 class c heavy duty wrecker class c wreckers for towing vehicles in excess of 17000 pounds large trucks road tractortrailers and similar vehicles shall meet the following minimum requirements a truck chassis having a minimum gross vehicle weight rating gvwr of not less than 46000 pounds b tandem axles or cab to axle length of not less than 102 inches c a single or double boom with a capacity of not less than 50000 pounds as rated by the manufacturer d a single winch with a capacity of 50000 pounds as rated by the manufacturer or an individual power winch capacity of not less than 25000 pounds as rated by the manufacturer and a total rating with both winches of 50000 pounds e a manufactured wheellift with a retracting lifting capacity of not less than 12000 pounds as rated by the manufacturer with safety chains f a minimum of 200 feet of fiveeightsinch cable or larger plus 50 feet of fiveeightsinch drop cable g airbrakes constructed so as to lock wheels automatically upon failure h light and air brake hookups i comealongs chains or other similar devices shall not be used as substitutes for winch and cable j additional safety equipment as specified by the regulations b additional requirements every wrecker to be placed on the valley police department wrecker rotation list regardless of class shall meet the following standards 1 all equipment necessary for the towing vehicle or combination of towing vehicle and towed vehicle must comply with the requirements of cfr 39 parts 390399 of the federal motor carrier rules and regulations when applicable 2 must be well maintained and in good conditions at all times and comply with all applicable state federal and local laws 3 each wrecker shall have the following standard equipment at all times a tow bars b two or more safety chains c a minimum of two class c fire extinguishers mounted in an accessible location class c extinguishers should not be used around electricity and if used around gas the gas supple should be isolated each wrecker company is responsible for following all safety precautions relating to fir extinguishing d one wrecking bar or pry bar with a minimum length of 30 inches e a minimum of three flares of at least 15 minutes duration or triangle reflectors f one pushtype broom g one flat shovel h one axe i one pair of bolt cutters with a minimum opening of onehalf inch j a minimum of 40 pounds of sand or absorbent material k a yellow or amber rotating or strobe light or light bar shall be affixed about the top of the can of the wrecker the warning lights shall be visible from 360 degrees and a distance of not less than 1500 feet under normal atmospheric conditions at night sirens are prohibited l dual rear adjustable floodlights with a minimum of 20000 candlepower each are required m one pair of magnetically mounted tow lights to be mounted at rear of towed vehicle see 325a134h class a conventional and class b only n every wrecker must display a currant license plate of the proper classification o every wrecker shall have displayed in lower right corner of the passengers windshield a departmental decal indicating a current inspection and eligibly to be on rotation log p the name address and telephone number of the wrecker company shall be permanently affixed to both sides of the wrecker using letters and numerals which are clearly visible from a distance of 100 feet the lettering used for the company name shall be at least four inches high and the lettering and numerals used for the address and telephone shall be at least tow inches q reserved r the wrecker company shall not place or imprint on their vehicles building equipment clothing or correspondence anything that suggests or implies any official relationship between the wrecker company and any law enforcement agency specifically paint colorsschemes similar to department vehicles  any decals similar in design to department decals  or any name or logo such as city wrecker are specifically forbidden c in addition to the above requirements of subsection b class c wreckers as defined in this regulation are required to be equipped with the following items 1 two chock blocks to prevent rolling or slippage of wrecker these chock blocks should have the capability of being tied to the wrecker and of a width equal to that of the dual wheels of the wrecker 2 at least six safety cones or triangle reflectors d nothing in these regulations is meant to preclude innovative wrecker or auto recovery equipment or vehicles such new equipment may be considered for use by companies included on the wrecker rotation list upon written request directed to the chief of police  ii 1122009  applications a general each wrecker company desiring to be placed on the valley police department wrecker rotation list shall complete an application for placement on rotation list wrecker information sheet driver information sheet and agreement & waiver form all forms will be submitted to the chief of police 1 the valley police department will furnish each wrecker company making a request to be placed on the rotation list a copy of the rules forms regulations and laws pertaining to the operations of wreckers included on a valley police department rotation list 2 the applicant will furnish the valley police department chief of police with a copy of certificate of insurance and casualty coverage as defined in section 46151 definitions this form must be signed by an authorized agent 3 the chief of police or designee shall conduct an investigation of the requesting wrecker company and determine if the business meets all qualifications that are required to be placed on the valley police department rotation list 4 the investigating officer will inspect all equipment that is to be used by the wrecker company and determine if it complies will all applicable laws and regulations in addition the investigating officer will conduct a preliminary background investigation of all operations covered in sections 46157 and 46158 heshe will submit the completed investigation to the chief of police 5 when the chief of police is satisfied the wrecker company is qualified heshe will issue the wrecker company and authorization permit and place the company on the valley police department rotation list 6 the investigating officer will place a department decal on each wrecker passing the inspection this decal will be affixed to the lower right corner of the passenger window to indicate current inspection and eligibility to be in the rotation list 7 a wrecker company that fails to pass inspection and qualification as prescribed by regulation will be notified of the deficiencies when the wrecker company corrects the deficiencies it may request a new inspection 8 authorization permits shall be considered personal to the holder thereof and shall be issued only to some definite legal business operating a wrecker service and shall not be subject to lease nor shall the holder thereof sublet to permit the exercise by another in any manner of the rights or privileges granted there under 9 an annual inspection will be conducted of the wrecker companys place of business storage facility and all trucks and towing equipment 10 any wrecker company that adds a new wrecker to its fleet will submit a wrecker information sheet for that vehicle to the chief of police it must then pass an inspection before being used on any rotation call  iii 1122009  insurance each operator from the time he moves or otherwise makes contact with any other vehicle to be towed assumes liability for injury to persons damage to property fires or theft resulting from the operators movement or other contact each operator shall maintain an insurance policy issued by an insurer with a current authorization from the alabama department of insurance to issue policy the operator shall main the following policies of insurance 1 workers compensation insurance as required by current statute 2 liability insurance on wreckers and business premises in an amount not less than $30000000 for a class a wrecker $50000000 for a class b wrecker and $7000000 for a class c wrecker 3 onhook insurance that covers vehicles cargo and other property in or on the vehicle during transit in an amount of not less that $7500000 for a class a wrecker $15000000 for a class b wrecker and $25000000 for a class c wrecker 4 garagestorage keepers liability insurance covering customers vehicles in an amount not less that $10000000 for an class a wrecker $20000000 for a class b wrecker and $20000000 for a class c wrecker a a maximum deductible of $100000 per occurrence b each policy required hereunder shall contain an endorsement providing for 30 days notice to the chief of police prior to any material change therein andor cancellation thereof c a copy of the certificate if insurance and casualty coverage is to be filed with the chief of police the valley police department will be listed as a certificate holder under all polices under this section  iv 1122009  wrecker rotation listcall allocation system the chief of police shall set up a wrecker rotation system that best meets the needs and best serves the valley police department the rotation system guidelines are set forth follows 1 to be eligible for approval to tow in the city or its police jurisdiction the wrecker operators place of business and storage facility must be located in chambers county however except that if there are no qualified operators in a particular area the chief of police may designate qualified outofcounty wrecker operators to be called into that area 2 wrecker company operators shall be placed on the rotation list in order of application and will be called for service and for removal o a wrecked disabled stolen impounded or abandoned vehicle according to the operators placement on wrecker rotation list 3 the wrecker company must have a wrecker of sufficient size and strength to handle the job the valley police department reserves the right not to use a wrecker company that in its opinion fails to meet this qualification for a specific job under these conditions the wrecker service not called will remain on the top of the rotation list 4 a wrecker company may respond with a wrecker of a higher class than requested however the wrecker company is limited to the rates of the requested classification 5 a wrecker company may not assign transfer pledge surrender encumber or dispose his place on the rotation wrecker list the wrecker company agrees to respond to all calls requested by the valley police department 24 hours a day seven days a week if for any reason an operator cannot respond he will be logged as unavailable operators who refuse to respond or develop a pattern of not responding to calls shall be subject to suspension or removal from the chief of police 6 in the event the call is an owners request if the department cancels the call or a response is made without rendering service the wrecker company will not be marked as unavailable on the list 7 a wrecker company will be listed on each wrecker rotation list only once this listing will use the name of the wrecker company submitted during the application process and which they were qualified under it is prohibited for a wrecker operator conducting business at one location to receive multiple listings or classifications by utilizing a different or fictitious name for trucks operating from the same location or by utilizing trucks with the same name out of a different location wrecker companies or corporations operating more that one rotation wrecker business within the same county or city or in more that one county or city must maintain completely separate officers required paperwork logs and assigned rotation wreckers at the approved location each business must have at least one wrecker available for call for each city approved for attempts to circumvent the intent of the rotation system will result in the removal for a period of not less than five years 8 when emergency conditions necessitate the department reserves the right to request the services of the wrecker company or operator who is the best able to handle the emergency and can reach the scene in the shortest time regardless of the operators position on the rotation list if a call us made under these circumstances this call will count as that wreckers next rotation call 9 whenever heavy equipment or large vehicles are involved in an accident and is determined that the wrecker next up in the rotation list does not have adequate to handle the accident then the department reserves the right to call a large wrecker from an operator on the list that can handle the situation if a call is made under these circumstances the operator will be repositioned accordingly call for large wreckers will be rotated around the companies having qualified larger wreckers having only on large rotation wrecker is not justification for being called to all truck accidents example an overturned truck usually requires more than one wrecker or specialized recovery equipment the valley police department would call the rotation company capable of solely handing the truck recovery  v 1122009 operations a wrecker companies will provide to the department a list of all wrecker operator personnel including their full name current address date of birth drivers license number and social security number each wrecker operator shall be investigated regarding any criminal history any criminal history of an operator which affects the companys qualification for the job shall be grounds for rejection of the wrecker company b the chief of police will conduct an annual review of the records of the wrecker companies and operators on the wrecker rotation list to determine if any convictions of crimes which would impact on the individuals qualifications to remain on the wrecker rotation list have occurred since their initial inclusion in addition to the annual review the chief of police will conduct random inspections of as many current owneroperator records as manpower and time restrictions will permit c before any newly hired employee of the wrecker company is allowed to drive a wrecker for any rotation call the wrecker company who is currently on a wrecker rotation list will furnish the chief of police with a criminal and drivers history of the new employee the chief of police will notify the wrecker company owner if the new hire us approved upon receipt of said histories d each company must have the proper business license issued by all applicable governing bodies and provide the valley police department with copies e no wrecker company owner or operator shall be on the rotation list who maintains a reputation in the community of associating with convicted felons who tolerates or condones gambling the drinking of alcoholic beverages or the use of illicit drugs in or about the business premises  or who allows any other activity that imparts a poor reputation upon the business f no wrecker company employees shall be on the rotation list unless the wrecker company employee is proficient and competent in the operations of the wreckers used it will be the responsibly of the business owner to ensure that all drivers and wrecker company operators are trained in the safe operation of vehicles and equipment used wrecker company operators will be removed form the rotation that demonstrate a lack of proficiency or respond with inadequate equipment g each wrecker company will furnish the chief of police with one telephone number to be used for requests for service during the day and one telephone number to be used for requests for service during the night or on weekends immediate notification shall be made to the chief of police if there is any change in the aforementioned telephone numbers call forwarding which provides immediate contact with the owneroperator is permitted answering services pager systems or any communications system will be allowed at the discretion of the chief of police h no operator shall proceed to the scene of an accident without being requested to do so by a law enforcement officer or agent of the valley police department or when requested by a member of his own wrecker company to assist as outlined in these regulations this is not to be constructed as subcontracting wrecker company operator shall not solicit business at the scene of an accident solicitation shall not include referral for repairreplacement of an auto or referral for any legal service no wrecker company operator will accept requests for services unless that operator had a vehicle immediately available to perform the requested service i no wrecker company operator shall speed or violate any other traffic laws or disregard any traffic control device while answering a call nor upon arrival needlessly congest the scone of the wreck j wreckers dispatched must arrive to the scene within 30 minutes if the time to reach the scene exceeds the above limits and the wrecker company does not notify the valley police department dispatcher of a valid reason for a delay with the said time a second wrecker may be requested of the second wrecker is requested before the arrival of the first rotation wrecker the initially requested wrecker will forfeit the call and will immediately leave the collisionincident scene k repeated tardiness will result in suspension or removal from the valley police department wrecker rotation list l additional requirements 1 the investigating officer at the scene of a collision had the right to designate which vehicle will be towed by a certain wrecker the wrecker operator first on the scene may have first choice of vehicle unless other wise directed by the officer 2 at no time shall any tow truck exceed its manufacturers gvwr or the manufacturers rated capacity for the towing assembly not be attached to a vehicle which by its size andor weight would male towing said vehicle an unsafe movement 3 it shall be the responsibilities of the wrecker company to perform a general cleanup of the accident area before leaving the scene of any accident this responsibility requires the wrecker company to remove all debris such as broken glass liquids and materials from an accident area by sweeping up such debris and removing this material from the scene 4 each wrecker company shall be responsible for securing personal property in a vehicle at an accident scene the wrecker company shall be responsible for preserving personal property in a vehicle towed from an accident scene 5 any officer acting in his official capacity may direct the wrecker company operator to take the vehicle being towed to the valley police department facility or designated facility for examination in furtherance of an official investigation this may include multiple vehicles towed by different companies to be stored at one wrecker facility in this case the towed vehicles will be taken to and stored at the facility of the first operator to arrive on the scene unless otherwise directed by the investigating officer 6 all towing and recovery services who tow and store vehicles which have been abandoned upon a highway will abide by the requirements as stated in 32131 thru 8 alabama 1975 and all applicable revenue codes vehicles towed and stored under these circumstances will be disposed of with 180 days of initial storage towing and recovery services will notify the valley police department immediately of the sale of any abandoned vehicles subcontracting is prohibited rotation wreckers may not subcontract wrecker calls this includes on scene operations in the event the on scene rotation wrecker is unable to handle the towing operation the officer will cancel that wrecker and a rotation wrecker capable of handling the operation will be called 7 all towing and recovery services will provide the department with its business tax id number fein and us dot numbers  vi 1122009  storage procedures a all wrecker companies and operators shall employ reasonable safeguards and procedures so all personal belongings and contents in the vehicle are intact and returned to the vehicles owner or agent upon vehicles from the police department d all operators of wrecker service on the rotation list shall reasonable permit during normal business hours and without charge the owner or owners designated representative of any vehicle stored upon or within the companies facilities to inspect the same remove items or personal belongings and the license plate there from in addition the wrecker company shall also reasonable permit and allow during normal business hours and with out charge insurance agents adjusters to enter inspect and photograph any such vehicle e in the event a stored vehicle has been placed on hold or impound as defined in this manual no access to the vehicle will be allowed without expressed permission from the chief of police or hisher designee this restriction shall not apply to access by a member if the department engaged in official duties department members will be allowed to access vehicles any anytime and said access will be without charge to either the department or vehicle owner f no vehicle shall be moved released or disposed of by a towingwrecker service without permission of the chief of police andor hisher designee  vii 1122009  rates and charges a wreckertowing services on the valley police department rotation list shall be subject to the following regulations 1 motorists utilizing the valley police department rotation list will have the option of paying by major credit card the wrecker company may request prior to dispatching if the motorist intends to pay by major credit card if the wrecker company does not accept major credit cards the next wreckertowing services which accepts credit cards will be utilized any wreckertowing service called that does not accept credit cards will remain on the top of the rotation list 2 fees charged for rotation list calls shall be set annually by the chief of police the fees charged and maximum limits will be determined in the following manner 3 all wreckertowing companies shall submit proposed fees annually to the chief of police for each class of wrecker and for each class the fee for standard towing heavyduty towing storage and special operations as describe below a a standard tow is defines as responding to the scene hooking up the vehicle performing a general clean up if the call involves responding to a collision scene and providing responsible assistance to the owner to get a safe location b special operations are operations involving the process of uprighting an overturned vehicle or returning a vehicle to a normal position on the roadway which requires the use of auxiliary equipment due to the size of location of the vehicle andor the recovery of a load which has spilled or the offloading and reloading of a load from an overturned vehicle performed to right the vehicle c any vehicle placed on hold as defined in section 46151 of this article shall not incur storage charges for the first 72 hours after being placed in storage after this time the daily storage rate submitted by the wrecker service shall apply d the chief of police will determine the reasonableness of the fees based upon the average of the proposed fees submitted and a comparison of industry standards for similar operations 4 a copy of the approved fees shall be in the wrecker at all times it shall be presented upon request of the person for whom the tow services were provided their agent any valley police officer at the scene andor any valley police department supervisor who is inspecting the wrecker or wrecker service 5 all wreckertowing companies shall submit proposed fees in writing to the chief of police by october 1st of each year the chief of police shall publish approved fees no later the december 31st to be effective january 1st of the following year 6 wrecker companies may lower rates at any time and may raise rates for nonvalley police department calls at any time however any company which engages in predatory business practices by charging fees which are excessive and outside industry standards shall be subject to removal from the wrecker rotation list and revocation of their business license b any wreckertowing service is subject to suspension andor removal from the wrecker rotation list if it is determined by the chief of police that a wreckertowing service has violated any section of the article while on a call derived from the wrecker rotation list c the maximum fees rates allowed are as follows vehicle day nightweekend  cleanup special operations storage cars 6500 12500 2500 30000 rollovers etc 2500 per day sport utility lbs + 25000 25000 4500 per hour 50000 per hour 5000 per day trucks tractor 25000 25000 4500 per hour 50000 per hour 5000 per day trucks tractortrailer 50000 50000 4500 per hour 50000 per hour 5000 per maintain a record system covering all services performed in pulling or towing all vehicles in conjunction with the valley police department rotation system and such records shall include the following 1 the date and time the operator was contacted and requested to perform his service 2 the name of the person requesting the service 3 the location of the vehicle 4 a description of the towed vehicle including license plate and identification number 5 the owner or driver of the vehicle if known 6 the service charge and fees 7 all records required herein must be available for inspection by officers or agents of the valley police department such inspection shall be conducted during normal business hours at the wrecker service or storage facility b the operator shall maintain the aforementioned records for the current calendar year and the calendar year immediately prior to the current calendar year c a record of all abandoned motor vehicles is to be maintained by the wrecker company and any abandoned motor vehicle sold or disposed of shall be done in accordance with ala 197 ch 13 noncompliance with the rules and regulations set forth herein will result in disciplinary action  ix 1122009  penalties a any violation of these regulations shall cause the removal of the owneroperator from the valley police department wrecker rotation list attempts to circumvent the intent of the rotation system and its policies will result in the removal of all wrecker companies and corporations related to the offending wrecker operator temporary suspensions shall be at the discretion of the chief of police and shall not be less than 60 days nor more than six months repeat or serious violations or violations of section 46169 rates and charges will result in the suspension from the rotation system for a period not less than one year and possible indefinite removal the offending wrecker company may reapply at the end of the suspension period 1 a wrecker company may upon receipt of a notification of suspension or removal from the wrecker rotation list submit a written request to the valley police department who will review the facts and schedule a hearing such written request must be received by the department within ten calendar days after the operator receives notification this will start the suspensionremoval from the wrecker rotation list pending final disposition provided that allowing the owneroperator to remain on the list would not endanger public safety if desired the wrecker companys legal counsel may be present at the hearing but will not take an active role in the proceedings if counsel is present the city attorney may participate to aid and assist the chief of police 2 any applicant who does not qualify to receive and authorization permit may submit a written request to the chief of police for a hearing regarding the denial such request must be made within ten calendar days after the applicant receives notice of not qualifying 3 the department shall reinstate to the rotation list any suspended owner operator upon written application after the period of suspension has elapsed and after the department has determined such operator is in compliance with all regulations pertaining to the valley police department rotation wrecker system 4 any applicant that feels that their appeal has not been addressed appropriately may appeal to the mayor within peddling it shall be unlawful for any person in the city to allow the house or building in which the people live or own or the premises around the house or the alley or street abutting the premises to become or remain in an unsanitary or unsightly condition a enforcement this provision shall be enforced by the city code enforcement officer who upon finding that this section is being violated shall issue written notification to the last party assessing the property for state taxes to the address on file in the tax office by certified or registered mail the mailing of the certified or registered mail notice properly addressed and postage prepaid shall constitute notice as required by this section in addition a copy of the notice is also posted at the property site the notice shall require the violation to be corrected within 14 days of the date of the notice the owner or person assessing the property for taxes shall have the right to file a written request for a hearing before the city council on this notice provided that the request is made in writing to the city clerk within 14 days of the notice this notice shall be required to sets forth any objections to the finding by the city official b action if appeal is made if an appeal is made within the allotted time the city council shall hear the report together with any objections which may be raised by any owner whose property is liable to be assessed for the work and the council may make such modifications in the report as they deem necessary after which by resolution the report may be confirmed or denied if the report is confirmed the council shall allow the owner ten days to address the violation should the violation not be addressed within this time the council may authorize the code enforcement officer to abate the violation by cleaning the property and removing any trash or other violating condition from the property the code enforcement officer of the city shall coordinate an effort to go upon the property and address the abatement utilizing city services or contracting for the service after completion of this work the code enforcement officer shall render an itemized report to the council showing the cost incurred in abating the nuisance upon the filing of this cost a public hearing shall be held for consideration thereof with notice being given to the person assessing the property for taxes by first class mail at the public hearing if the council may approve the report of the code enforcement office and pass a resolution assessing a lien against the property for the recovery of the costs of abatement c action if no appeal is made if no request for hearing is made within the time required and the violation has not been corrected the code enforcement officer shall appear before the council and render his written report of the violation upon considering the report the council may find that the violation of the section exists and may authorize the code enforcement officer to abate the violation by cleaning the property and removing any trash or other violating condition from the property the code enforcement officer of the city shall coordinate an effort to go upon the property and address the abatement utilizing city services or contracting for the service after completion of this work the code enforcement officer shall render an itemized report to the council showing the cost incurred in abating the nuisance upon the filing of this cost a public hearing shall be held for consideration thereof with notice being given to the person assessing the property for taxes by first class mail at the public hearing if the council may approve the report of the code enforcement office and pass a resolution assessing a lien against the property for the recovery of the costs of abatement d lien assessment the amounts of the costs for the abating of a violation of this section shall constitute special assessments against the land and as thus made and confirmed shall constitute a lien on the property for the amount of such assessment thereafter such amounts shall be collected at the same time and in the same manner as ordinary municipal assessments are collected and shall be subject to the same penalties a copy of the resolution shall also be filed in the office of the probate court of chambers county alabama imposing a lien on the property e criminal penalty the code enforcement officer or any law enforcement officer may issue a citation to the owner and occupant of the property upon which the violation exists requiring the person to appear in municipal or district court to answer charges for the violation of this section such citation shall name the party charged the address of the property where the alleged violation is located and the nature of the offense or violation it shall also apprise the person of the date time and place at which to appear in court such citation returnable to the municipal or district court shall be served on the owner of the property by any code enforcement officer for the city instead of placing a person under custodial arrest may issue a summons and complaint against a person charged with a violation of this section for purposes of this section the city authorizes the use of the uniform nontraffic citation and complaint form currently utilized by the city the procedure for issuing a citation is that when an arrest is to be made the arresting officer releases the person upon his written promise to appear in court at the designated time and place if the person refuses to sign the citation and appear in court the officer is to take the person into custody and bring him before any officer or official authorized to approve a bond f means of enforcement the code enforcement officer or any law enforcement officer may institute either or both enforcement procedures set forth above the institution of one procedure does not preclude the subsequent or simultaneous institution of the other procedure provided the criminal procedure is not used to collect any outstanding civil assessments against the subject property g penalties any person violating any provisions hereof shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and upon conviction shall be fined not less than $5000 nor more than $20000 and if the violation or failure or refusal to obey or comply with such section is a continuing one each days violation shall constitute a separate offense and shall be punished accordingly  14 572018 secs 5055030  reserved article ii  nuisances household appliances and household furniture prohibited outside any dwelling or business the following rules and regulations for prohibiting outside storage of appliances and household furniture outside any dwelling or business within the city limits of valley are hereby adopted 1 it shall be unlawful for any person residing in or having charge or control of any dwelling or any person occupying using or having control of any business within the city to leave or permit to remain outside of any such dwelling or business any household appliances or household furniture in such a manner that the same are exposed to the elements 2 household appliances and household furniture are defined as those items routinely used within a household or business related to the occupancy thereof examples of household appliances and furniture may include but are not limited to the following refrigerators washing machines clothes dryers freezers dishwashers sofas cushioned chairs not intended for outdoor use dressers bureaus dining room and kitchen tables and any other appliance or article of furniture not normally intended for outdoor use or exposure to the elements 3 elements is defined as those aspects of inclement weather conditions for which such items are not designed nor intended to function or exist for extended periods of time such as rain wind and temperature extremes normally associated with outdoor conditions 4 exposed is defined as circumstances under which such items will experience excessive wear and tear due to their location out of doors andor the deleterious effects of the elements such that water may accumulate andor which may shelter andor encourage the harboring of rodents andor mosquitoes andor materials which generate obnoxious odors andor become an electrical shock or fire hazard exposed expressly does not include an operating appliance in working condition located in a partially covered area such as a garage or rear porch such that it is not susceptible to coming in contact with rain or any other elements provided however that exposed shall not include the interior of any fully enclosed porch including without limitation a porch enclosed by screening material that cannot be accessed from outside except closed door that can be locked and shall not be considered outside for the purpose of this section 5 the following shall constitute specific defenses to any alleged violation of this provision a that such furniture was placed in an outside location in order to allow it to be moved during a move of a resident or residents or removed as part of a trash or recycling program on a day scheduled for such moving or removal b that such furniture was temporarily placed in an outside location in order that it be offered for sale at a yard or garage sale or as may be involved in a legitimate offer of sale by a business or merchant if each of the following conditions exists 1 the furniture is located in an outside location only during the hours of  am and  pm 2 the person attempting to sell the furniture or that persons agent is outside during the period of the yard or garage sale in order to monitor the sale or if such sale is conducted by a business or merchant a sales person is outside or in the applicable business premises 3 a sign is placed on or near the furniture indicating that it is for sale 4 this defense shall not apply if upholstered furniture is located in an outside location for more than two days in any sixmonth period 6 anyone found guilty of violation of this article shall be subject to the punishment set forth in section 111 of the ordinances   6272011  planning or regulation of the city of valley   4272009  definitions the following words and terms shall for the purposes of this chapter and as used elsewhere in this code have the meanings shown herein abandoned sign a sign structure that has ceased to be used and the owner intends no further use thereof animated sign a sign employing actual motion or the illusion of motion animated signs which are differentiated from changeable signs as defined and regulated by this include the following types 1 electrically activated animated signs producing the illusion of movement by means of electronic electrical or electromechanical input andor illumination capable of simulating movement of the characteristics of one or both of the classifications noted below a flashing animated signs or animated portions of signs whose illumination is characterized by a repetitive cycle in which the period of illumination is either the same as or less than the period of nonillumination for the purposes of this ordinance flashing will not be defined as occurring if the cyclical period between onoff phases of illumination exceeds four seconds b patterned illusionary movement animated signs or animated portions of signs whose illumination is characterized by simulated movement or sequential activation of various illuminated elements for the purpose of producing repetitive light patterns designed to appear in some form of constant motion 2 environmentally activated animated signs or devices motivated by wind thermal changes or other natural environmental input includes spinners pinwheels pennant strings andor other devices or displays that respond to naturally occurring external motivation 3 mechanically activated animated signs characterized by repetitive motion andor rotation activated by a mechanical system powered by electric motors or other mechanically induced means architectural projection any projection that is not intended for occupancy and that extends beyond the face of an exterior wall of a building but that does not include signs as defined herein see also awning  backlit awning  and canopy attached and freestanding awning an architectural projection or shelter projecting from and supported by the exterior wall of a building and composed of a covering of rigid or non rigid materials andor fabric on a supporting framework that may be either permanent or retractable including such structures that are internally illuminated by fluorescent or other light sources awning sign a sign displayed on or attached flat against the surface or surfaces of an awning see also wall or fascia sign backlit sign an awning with a translucent covering material and a source of illumination contained within its framework banner a flexible substrate on which copy or graphics may be displayed banner sign a sign utilizing a banner as its display surface billboard see offpremises sign and outdoor advertising sign building elevation the entire side of a building from ground level to the roofline as viewed perpendicular to the walls on that side of the building canopy attached a multisided overhead structure or architectural projection supported by attachments to a building on one or more sides and either cantilevered from such building or also supported by columns at additional points the surfaces andor soffit of an attached canopy may be illuminated by means of internal or external sources of light see also marquee canopy freestanding a multisided overhead structure supported by columns but not enclosed by walls the surfaces and or soffit of a freestanding canopy may be illuminated by means of internal or external sources of light canopy sign a sign affixed to the visible surfaces of an attached or freestanding canopy changeable sign a sign remote electrically energized onoff switching combinations of alphabetic or pictographic components arranged on a display surface illumination may be integral to the components such as characterized enterprise where the enterprise does not receive direct commercial gain 7 street address signs and combination nameplate and street address signs that contain no advertising copy and which do not exceed six square feet in area 8 political signs on private property   4272009  prohibited signs the following devices and locations shall be specifically prohibited 1 signs located in such a manner as to obstruct or otherwise interfere with an official traffic sign signal or device or obstruct or interfere with a drivers view of approaching merging or intersecting traffic 2 except as provided for elsewhere in this code signs encroaching upon or overhanging public rightofway no sign shall be attached to any utility pole light standard street tree or any other public facility located within the public rightofway 3 signs which blink flash or are animated by lighting in any fashion that would cause such signs to have the appearance of traffic safety signs and lights or municipal vehicle warnings from a distance 4 portable signs except as allowed for temporary signs 5 any sign attached to or placed on a vehicle or trailer parked on public or private property except for signs meeting the following conditions a the primary purpose of such a vehicle or trailer is not the display of signs b the signs are magnetic decals or painted upon an integral part of the vehicle or equipment as originally designed by the manufacturer and do not break the silhouette of the vehicle c the vehicle andor trailer is in operating condition currently registered and licensed to operate on public streets when applicable and actively used or available for use in the daily function of the business to which such signs relate 6 vehicles and trailers used primarily as static displays advertising a product or service utilized as storage shelter or distribution points for commercial products or services for the general public 7 balloons streamers or pinwheels except those temporarily displayed as part of a special sale promotion or community event for the purposes of this subsection temporarily means no more than 20 days in any calendar year   4272009  visibility no sign or sign structure shall be erected at the intersection of any street in such a manner as to obstruct free and clear vision nor at any location where by its position size shape color movement flashing or illumination may interfere with or obstruct the view of or be confused with any authorized traffic sign signal or device 1 in the forestryagriculturerecreation and in all residential districts signs may only be illuminated by nonflashing reflected light any light used to illuminate such signs shall be arranged so as to reflect light away from adjoining premises and streets 2 in commercial and industrial districts signs may be illuminated internally or by reflected light provided the source of light is not directly visible and is so arranged as to reflect light away from adjoining premises and streets no illumination involving movement by reason of the lighting arrangement or by other devices shall be permitted flashing lights shall not be permitted   4272009  computation of frontage if a premises in a residential district and for all commercial and industrial districts subject to the following limitations 1 such signs must be approved by the city plannerzoning administrator or code official shall be erected no more than five days prior to the event or grand opening and shall be removed not more than one day after the event or grand opening 3 the total area of all such signs shall not public property or obstruct traffic visibility no banner or sign shall be placed across or over any street or rightofway or alley   4272009  nonconformance of existing signs all existing sign that are not specifically permitted or that do not comply with all provisions of this ordinance shall be considered nonconforming signs and shall not after the effective date of this chapter be enlarged structurally altered of extended unless such signs shall be made to comply with all provisions of this section 1 normal repairs and repainting of nonconforming signs is permitted however when a nonconforming sign structurally needs repairing damaged or destroyed by any means to the extent of 50 percent or more of its replacement value exclusive of foundations it shall not thereafter be restored unless said sign shall be made to conform to all provisions of this chapter 2 all existing billboards located in any zoning district except as permitted in this chapter shall be considered nonconforming and shall be regulated in accordance with the provisions of this chapter 3 all existing portable signs located in all zoning districts shall be considered nonconforming and shall be removed no later than 90 days from the effective date of this chapter   4272009  political signs it is unlawful to place erect or maintain political signs earlier than 30 days prior to the official election date said signs must be removed within seven days after the official election date in the event of a runoff election the signs of the runoff candidates may be maintained until the seventh day after the runoff election political signs are limited in size to no more than 32 square feet pursuant to ala 197  2316 it shall be unlawful to place signs markers and advertising on the rights of way of state controlled highways except those official signs or markers placed thereon by the state department of transportation or under its authority it shall also be unlawful to erect or display political signs on any property owned or controlled by the city of valley this shall include public rightsofways trees light poles sidewalks streets benches fire hydrants public parks or playgrounds and city hall the valley city council may designate by resolution certain properties that will allow political sign placement during the time frame specified in this section it is the candidates responsibility to ensure that the volunteers and sign contractors who distribute and erect political signs during an election are doing so in compliance with this law candidates will be held responsible for violations any sign removed for violation of this ordinance will be disposed of by city personnel and not held political signs are exempt from permits   4272009  window signs window
